Completion of the Municipal Double-Decker Ferry Terminal

Installed yesterday at the Bund on Beijing Road

Magnificent and unparalleled

According to the Central News Agency, the double-decker ferry terminal newly built on the Bund of Beijing Road by the Municipal Ferry Management Office of the Shanghai Municipal Government's Xingye Trust Company has now been completed. The construction process and structural details are recorded as follows:

Construction Significance

The municipal ferry operates intra-city water transportation with accurate timing, stable and fast navigation, perfect equipment, and low fares. Therefore, in recent years, it has made rapid progress. The number of passengers has been increasing daily. Last year, the total number of passengers reached more than 11.1 million (an increase of 4 million compared to 1933). Recognizing the increasing demand, the office is constantly improving and expanding all its business equipment. Currently, the terminal equipment and traffic order at various municipal ferry terminals are well-organized. However, the bronze statue wharf on the Bund of Nanjing Road is the terminus of the long-distance route, and the number of passengers entering and leaving is particularly large. According to statistics for 1934, the number of ferry passengers boarding and disembarking at this terminal has reached more than 4 million. However, this terminal is for public use, and any ships can dock there. Passengers entering and leaving cannot be separated, and there is no shelter on top. Passengers waiting for the ferry are exposed to the elements, which is extremely painful in cold winters, hot summers, or windy and rainy weather. To maintain passenger safety and comfort, as well as the order of boarding and disembarking, the office decided to build a separate dedicated terminal.

Construction Process

The office decided to build a dedicated terminal, but lacked a suitable shoreline. After repeated consultations with the Public Works Department, the Public Works Department, after careful consideration, recognized that the municipal ferry is a public transportation undertaking with a large number of passengers, and that the construction of a dedicated terminal was indeed necessary to meet the needs. Therefore, they immediately agreed to move the original No. 15 wharf on the Bund of Beijing Road to the south, freeing up a suitable shoreline for the office to build a steel double-decker floating terminal and two floating bridges. The office immediately began the design, which took five months to complete. In June of last year, tenders were invited, and in early July, the contract was awarded to the He Xing Shipyard. It was completed yesterday. In total, the design and construction time has been one year.

Structure and Equipment

The construction of this double-decker floating terminal is extremely grand. From a distance, it resembles a mirage on the river. This type of construction is the first of its kind in Shanghai, and it is rare even in the Far East. It is 48.770 meters long, 9.145 meters wide, and 7.620 meters high, with a draft of 0.610 meters. Two ferries can dock at the terminal at the same time. The terminal building is entirely made of steel and surrounded by steel windows. The floating bridge at the north end of the lower level serves as the entrance, where ticket offices are set up, with five ticket windows: (1) for cross-river ferries, (2) for first-class long-distance ferries, (3) and (4) for second-class, and (5) for joint Shangchuan tickets. Opposite the ticket offices is a consumer cooperative, exchanging money, selling cigarettes, candy, and sundries. Because the store is operated by the office itself, it is designed to provide convenience for passengers and is not for profit. Prices are the lowest on the market. There is also a car rental agency, with special agreements with Xiang Sheng cars to pick up and drop off passengers, to facilitate travel. The middle part is the passenger waiting area. Long-distance and cross-river ferries are separated by iron fences to avoid confusion. Comfortable seats are provided for passengers to wait. In the waiting area, there are reading areas and tea rooms. The south end is the exit for passengers boarding the ferry. The upper level is the business office, with simple and unadorned interior equipment. There is also a special first-class ticket office and a first-class waiting area, an information desk, and an attached floating hotel, which specializes in serving the highest-quality Western cuisine for elegant ladies to entertain guests. It is not exclusively for passengers. Fees are low, and management is strict. The interior decoration is undertaken by the Times Company, which is solemn and elegant, rich but not extravagant. The dining room is surrounded by steel windows, with heating in winter and air conditioning in summer. The scenery on all sides is excellent. The location is superior, and the air is fresh, unmatched by any hotel on land. It is expected to open at the end of February, at which time the elegant ladies of Shanghai will surely be happy to patronize it, as this type of floating hotel is truly a first in Shanghai. First-class passengers board and disembark the ferry from the upper level. Other facilities, such as hygiene and fire protection, are exquisite and complete. The total cost of construction and various decoration equipment is approximately 100,000 yuan.

Vehicle Traffic

To facilitate traffic to and from the terminal and intermodal transportation, the Public Works Department has converted the grassland on the embankment into a semi-circular avenue for vehicles to enter and exit, and added wide sidewalks on both sides to allow pedestrians and vehicles to pass without hindrance. It is expected to be fully completed in about a week.

Hiring Porters

Because many passengers carry luggage and items, the office has hired porters who wear numbered uniforms and charge fixed fees. Ordinary items cost 8 copper coins per piece, and special items that require two people to carry cost 16 copper coins per piece. If there are additional demands or unsatisfactory service, passengers can report to the terminal manager at any time or submit a written report to the management office, and strict disciplinary action will be taken.

Commencement of Docking

The terminal has now been installed on the Bund of Beijing Road and is currently being arranged. It is expected to begin docking ferries within the next week. All long-distance ferries between Shanghai and Wusong, as well as cross-river ferries to the Chunjiang wharf in Pudong, will be relocated to the new terminal, it is said.

Miniature of the Shanghai Municipal Ferry Double-Decker Terminal

Public Works Department News

The Public Works Department's Information Office released information on the Public Works Department's improvements to passenger and cargo handling along the Huangpu River. The Huangpu River ferry, operated by the Municipal Government, has historically operated from the floating pier at the intersection of Nanjing Road. However, that pier also serves other passenger and cargo needs. Approximately a year ago, the Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities consulted with the Public Works Department to obtain permission for the Pujiang Ferry to set up a dedicated pier for the convenience of passengers. In March of last year, the Public Works Department passed a resolution to allow the construction of a double-decker pier opposite the intersection of Beijing Road, dedicated to ferry passengers. At the same time, the Public Works Department also decided to dedicate the two piers at the intersections of Nanjing Road and Jiujiang Road for the use of other passengers, and adopted the suggestion of the Director of Public Works to equip a larger pier south of the Customs House, so that goods from other piers could be transferred there for loading and unloading without causing congestion. According to the statistics from a ten-day period last year, the vehicles carrying goods to and from the piers at Beijing Road, Jiujiang Road, and Hankou Road included 294 trucks, 1,052 handcarts, and 272 carts. The goods loaded and unloaded that did not belong to the concession accounted for 24%, 10%, and 9.75% respectively. The chartered steamships at the Jiujiang Road pier operated an average of 63 times per day, and the number of passengers disembarking at the Nanjing Road pier averaged 11,100 per day, with a maximum of 27,500 on the busiest day. After the ferry improvements, it is estimated that there will be an average of 20,000 ferry passengers per day.

Completion of Liquidation of Chia Hua Bank

The balance sheet of assets and liabilities has been sent to the head office for review.

According to the Central News Agency, the Shanghai branch of the Hong Kong Chia Hua Bank, since the suspension of business and liquidation of the head office, also suspended business on the 5th, and appointed lawyer Song Yunhui and accountant Wang Sifang to announce the liquidation. It has been a week until yesterday. The liquidation work has been completed. It is certified that the amount owed to others is approximately 200,000 yuan, and the amount owed by others is 196,000 yuan. Therefore, it can be offset. Currently, the balance sheet of assets and liabilities has been sent to the Hong Kong head office by airmail. It is estimated that a response can be received from the head office within about one week. At least 50,000 to 60,000 yuan can be repaid to creditors in the shortest possible time. However, under the heading of amounts owed by others, there are one or two banks that are unwilling to pay because of their relationship with the head office, and it is necessary to wait for the negotiation with the head office's lawyer before a decision can be made. The branch believes that it is economically completely independent, so it has now negotiated with the banks based on reason, hoping that they can issue the funds immediately to repay the depositors. Furthermore, the resumption of business of the head office is indeed in active progress. Because the creditors have already discussed three measures for the bank to resume business, if these conditions can be approved by the shareholders' meeting, the resumption of business will not be a problem, it is said.

Trade Associations Including Cigarette Exchange Submit a Joint Petition to the Finance Bureau Requesting Maintenance of Original Quotas

Various trade associations, including the Cigarette Exchange, Native Yellow Wine, Soy Sauce Garden, Soy Sauce and Wine, Shaoxing Wine, Fen Wine, and Wine Restaurant Associations, submitted a joint petition to the Finance Bureau yesterday, stating: "The petition is for requesting consideration of the merchants' difficulties and maintaining the original quotas, and requesting approval. It is found that the members of our associations engage in the cigarette and wine business and comply with regulations to apply for licenses and pay quarterly. During each tax collection period, they go to the collection agencies to pay taxes and obtain licenses. If they are overdue, the collection agencies send personnel to collect the taxes, adding a late fee of 10% to 20%. This has been the practice in the past, and the tax merchants have found it convenient. Since this year, it has been changed to be collected by the sub-bureaus of your bureau. Regardless of whether it is within or outside the time limit, merchants must go to the office to apply for licenses. If they are overdue, they are subject to heavy fines according to Article 8, Paragraph 1. In addition, there are frequent increases in various licenses. For example, those who have already obtained a Class C formal license in the autumn are upgraded to Class B in the winter. Now that rural areas are bankrupt and various industries are in decline, the consumption of cigarettes and alcohol has reached its end. Business is sluggish, which is self-evident. We are considering requesting a reduction in the original quotas. In addition, most of the stores in the two industries are operated by husband and wife and do not hire employees. Each tax collection period has a limited time of only ten days. Once it is overdue, heavy fines follow. Merchants feel the suffering of heavy taxes and the pain of heavy fines. How can we small merchants bear it? Our associations are representatives of the industry, and our purpose is to maintain the welfare of our members, to alleviate their suffering, and to seek their benefits. We have to make a request on their behalf. We request that your bureau order the tax collection offices to maintain the original quotas and not to increase them arbitrarily when tax collection begins in the spring. Late applications should still be subject to a late fee of 10% to 20% according to the ministerial regulations, and not to apply the strict measures of Article 8, Paragraph 1. We also request that personnel be dispatched outside the limited time to urge tax collection, so as to benefit small merchants and avoid heavy fines. This method will benefit both tax collectors and merchants. We hereby jointly submit a petition requesting your bureau's approval and requesting that the instructions be followed. This will be in the public interest."

Baoying People vs. Yancheng People

Three Injured, One in Critical Condition

The Jiangbei gang dock workers from Baoying and Yancheng near the pier of the Yongyu Yarn Factory in the Caogjiadu and Beishi Limestone Kiln areas of West Shanghai had accumulated grievances due to competing for work and demanding wages. At around 8:00 a.m. yesterday, both sides invited dozens of people, armed with axes, iron rods, wooden sticks, and bayonets, and started a full-scale fight with a shout. The Public Works Department will Implement Traffic Improvements Next Monday

Regulations on Turning at Intersections

The Public Works Department issued a notice yesterday, stating: "Notice is hereby given that the following new traffic regulations have been approved and will take effect from January 14, 1935 (Monday):

Article 46 (A)

Except on Sundays and public holidays, from 8:30 a.m. to 9:30 a.m., 12:00 p.m. to 12:30 p.m., 1:30 p.m. to 2:30 p.m., and 4:30 p.m. to 6:00 p.m., drivers shall not turn right from the intersection of Tibet Road and Nanjing Road onto Jing'an Temple Road.

Article 46 (B)

Except on Sundays and public holidays, from 8:30 a.m. to 9:30 a.m., 12:00 p.m. to 12:30 p.m., 1:30 p.m. to 2:30 p.m., and 4:30 p.m. to 6:00 p.m., drivers shall not turn right from the intersection of Tibet Road and Nanjing Road onto Nanjing Road.

Article 48 (A)

Except on Sundays and public holidays, from 12:00 p.m. to 1:00 p.m., and 4:30 p.m. to 6:00 p.m., all vehicles shall not stop or park directly or horizontally on the south side of the section of Jing'an Temple Road between Tibet Road and Maohuo Road.

Article 48 (B)

Except on Sundays and public holidays, from 12:00 p.m. to 12:30 p.m., 1:30 p.m. to 2:30 p.m., and 4:30 p.m. to 5:30 p.m., all vehicles shall not stop or park directly or horizontally on the west side of the section of Henan Road between Hankou Road and Fuzhou Road.

Article 48 (C)

Except on Sundays and public holidays, from 8:00 a.m. to 6:00 p.m., all vehicles shall not stop or park directly or horizontally on the east side of the section of Jiangxi Road between Hankou Road and Fuzhou Road.

Hua Yi Insurance Company Established

Hua Yi Insurance Company, located at No. 17 Bund, officially announced its establishment yesterday. The company operates on a general agency system, organized by two insurance experts: Mr. Lu Zirang and Mr. Dai Linzao, formerly the general manager and manager of the life insurance department of Taishan Insurance Company. They specialize in planning life, fire, and other types of insurance for clients. It is said that this type of general insurance agency system is unprecedented in the country. Messrs. Lu and Dai graduated from the University of Pennsylvania in the United States ten years ago, as top students of Professor Huebner. In the past few years, Mr. Lu has successively held important positions such as manager and general manager at New York Life Insurance Company, Shanghai AIA Life Insurance Company, and Taishan Insurance. Messrs. Lu and Dai have collaborated for many years. Before the new company was established, Mr. Dai served as the manager of the life insurance department of Taishan Insurance Company. According to Mr. Lu yesterday, the services and systems of Hua Yi Insurance Company are innovative in the country. The company issues various insurance policies from Sihai Insurance Company. Before clients decide on the type of insurance, the company engages in detailed discussions and research with them, so that each client can obtain the policy that best suits their needs. Mr. Lu also stated that today, intellectuals in the country have generally recognized the benefits of life insurance protection. Therefore, it is especially important to establish this type of business that is most popular in Western countries.

Foreigners Robbed by Bandits at the Junction of Haiyan and Haining on the Shanghai-Hangzhou Highway, Between Zhouliyan and Huangwan

Two bandits robbed 83 foreign dollars.

Police and others dispatched armed police to pursue.

Hangzhou Electric Telegram: Mr. Macnaghten, Deputy Chairman of the Shanghai Municipal Council, traveled from Shanghai to Hangzhou in his own car at 11:00 this morning. When he arrived at the junction of Haiyan and Haining, between Zhouliyan and Huangwan, he was suddenly attacked by two bandits. One bandit wore a gray long gown and a melon-shaped hat, was about 20 years old, and spoke with a Jiangbei accent. The other bandit had a festering middle finger. They robbed him of 83 foreign dollars. After the robbery, the bandits fired a gun as a warning and fled south. After the incident, the Public Security Bureau and Ma Ruifang, Chief Inspector of the Shanghai-Hangzhou Highway Patrol, dispatched fully armed police officers to the scene to investigate and are currently pursuing them.

Habitual Extortion of Shops by Threatening with Bombs

Claiming to be a member of the Iron-Blooded Assassination Corps

Repeated offenses lead to a seven-year sentence

Zhou Taibing (22 years old), a native of Zhenjiang, lived at No. 19 Yangzhou Road. At 8:45 PM on the 21st of last month, he went to Wanchangxiang Foreign Goods Store at No. 45 Huade Road with a bomb and purchased six pieces of silk fabric worth 52 foreign dollars. He claimed to be a member of the Iron-Blooded Assassination Corps, sent from Beijing. He said that the office was located at Yongji Lane, Fangbang Bridge, in the Chinese area and that the store was selling inferior goods, which needed to be taken for inspection. He then used the bomb to intimidate the shop and fled with the goods. Shop assistants Jiang Heming and Chen Jisheng bravely pursued him to Zhoushan Road, where they were intercepted by Chinese detective Liu Baoshan and two Chinese constables, No. 414 and No. 3001. They were taken to the Huishan Police Station along with the bomb and sent to the First Special District Court. His statement was evasive, and he was detained for further investigation. During the investigation, the Chinese and foreign detectives handling the case found that the defendant had used the same means to extort silk fabrics and jewelry worth more than 200 yuan from Tongfengyu at No. 530 Lixi Huade Road, Dehoufu at No. 478 Huade Road, Guangda at No. 215 Hubei Road, Yuhe on Fujian Road, and Lao Baohua Silver Shop at No. 328 Aivin Yi Road from March to December last year. He pawned the items for cash. The original stolen goods were recovered. Yesterday morning, the police station sent the Zhou offender back to the Third Criminal Court. Lawyer Li Zhishan from the Public Works Department described the previous situation in detail and stated that the bomb had been soaked in water to eliminate its explosive properties. Subsequently, the bomb was placed in a remote area 50 yards away and shot with a bullet. Experts had verified that it had the potential to explode. The internal blasting mechanism of the bomb was presented for inspection. The defendant had also used the same method on Gongguanma Road in the French Concession to intimidate a foreign goods store at No. 326, extorting silk fabrics worth 79.5 foreign dollars. The French police station had sent foreign detectives to request the transfer of the case. The defendant, under the guise of patriotism, used this type of explosive to intimidate various shops, extorting money and disrupting social order. He should be severely punished. Subsequently, the victims testified about the circumstances of the defendant's threat and the taking of goods. The French foreign detectives also submitted official documents requesting the transfer of the case. The defendant fully admitted to the charges. Judge Xiao Xieqiu sentenced Zhou Taibing to seven years in prison. The number of days of pre-trial detention will be deducted from the sentence at a rate of two days for each day of imprisonment. The bomb was confiscated and handed over to the Second Special District Court of Shanghai for transfer and trial, and then sent back for execution.

Ni Yunlai, Who Offered a Bribe, Was Apprehended

Sent to Caohejing Prison for Execution

Xielong Real Estate Company and Daxing Real Estate Company were previously involved in a property lawsuit in the First Special District District Court, which was being heard by Judge Shen Hongcheng of the Civil Division. Ni Yunlai, the manager of Xielong, while the case was still being heard, suddenly placed 1,000 yuan in cash in an envelope and sent it to Judge Shen's residence at No. 8 Xudong Lane, Tongfu Road, West Shanghai, in an attempt to bribe him and win the case. At that time, Judge Shen was working at the court. Mrs. Shen accepted the envelope, saw that it contained banknotes and a short note, and was about to question the messenger, but the person had already taken the opportunity to escape. She then asked Judge Shen to return to his residence and informed him of what had happened. Judge Shen immediately took the original item to the President of the Court, ordered the bribe envelope to be sent to the Inspection Office for investigation, and filed a public prosecution against Ni Yunlai for bribery. After several court hearings in the Criminal Division of the First Special Court, Ni, after being released on bail, fled in fear of punishment, so he could not be arrested. Although Ni Yunlai was sentenced to six months imprisonment and fined 3,000 yuan, the sentence could not be executed for a long time. It was not until October last year that President Guo Yunguan ordered a nationwide arrest warrant and offered a reward of 1,000 foreign dollars, hoping that people from all walks of life would help capture him. Although Ni's original residence was in Zhenhai, Ningbo, he owned a lot of property in Shanghai. Since committing the crime, he had not fled far away. Recently, Police Chief Lu Liankui and foreign inspector Kuer learned that Ni was hiding at No. 19 Yuyuan Road. Therefore, at 10:20 AM the day before yesterday, they led Chinese detective Wang Cheng and detective Bao Lisheng to the place and arrested Ni. Yesterday morning, he was escorted to the Criminal Execution Court of the First Special Court. Judge Shen Shanzeng brought the prisoner to court and questioned him about his name, age, place of origin, address, and occupation. Ni immediately requested not to be sent to the Tilanqiao West Prison, but to be sent to Jiangsu Second Prison in Caohejing for imprisonment. Judge Shen, considering that the prisoner's request was feasible, immediately approved it. Before the transfer documents were completed, he ordered Ni Yunlai to be temporarily detained in the Civil Custody Office. Ni is now 41 years old and has been doing business in Shanghai. In recent years, his business has been very prosperous, so he has become a wealthy man. He usually lives in comfort, but now, due to a moment of misjudgment, he has been convicted and imprisoned. Even if he wants to regret it, it is already too late.

Old Man and Young Woman Divorce

Chen Yuanzhang and Zhu Meizhen both unwilling to live together

Asking the matchmaker to make a formal adjustment of ages

Lawyer Qian Yuan denies writing the marriage certificate and participating

Chen Yuanzhang started his career by running a hardware business, accumulated a lot of wealth, and became a wealthy businessman. Chen is already sixty-five years old, and coupled with his frail physique, he appears even older. However, because he is getting better in his old age, his interest remains strong. In his spare time, he relies on his old eyes to look at flowers in the mist. In the summer, he met a young widow from Nanxiang named Zhu Meizhen. Chen was greatly pleased. The woman was in the prime of her life and had recently become a widow. Chen asked to form an alliance until their hair turned white, saying that he possessed 100,000 yuan in family wealth and would not treat her poorly if she agreed. The woman's heart was not a dry well, and she was moved by his words. Knowing that Chen was already old and frail, she sought a better life and did not mind remarrying. Therefore, Chen rented a room on the second floor above the street at No. 26, a certain lane on Mintiniyin Road in the French Concession and began living together. After a considerable period, they both felt that their personalities were compatible and began preparing for the wedding. Chen's neighbor, Pan Defan, a native of Ningbo, was a close friend of Chen's. Chen asked him and Zhang Fulai to act as matchmakers to handle the formalities. He also asked Ji Wenwei, a secretary of Lawyer Qian Yuan, to ask Lawyer Qian to draft the marriage certificate. They chose an auspicious day, July 12, to hold the wedding ceremony at the Dahonglou Restaurant on Wuma Road. However, Chen Yuanzhang, considering his advanced age and marrying a young woman, feared that not only would onlookers criticize him for "a pear blossom tree weighing down a crabapple," but also his family and friends would disapprove. Therefore, in the marriage certificate, he reduced his age by ten years, changing it from sixty-five to fifty-five, and increased Zhu Meizhen's age by four years, raising it to twenty-nine, to adjust and conceal the situation. Unexpectedly, after the marriage, Chen's attitude gradually changed. His generosity towards the woman in the past turned into miserliness. Although the woman was in charge of the household, the daily food expenses for her nine-member family were limited to only one thousand cash, causing the woman to often lament that "a clever housewife cannot cook without rice." When she asked Chen to increase the food expenses, Chen not only refused but also started arguing. The couple lived together for three and a half months, and quarrels were frequent. On October 25, the woman, unable to bear the situation, quietly returned to her mother's home in Nanxiang alone. After the woman left, Chen reported the incident to the police station, accusing the woman of absconding. On the other hand, he hired a lawyer to file a lawsuit against Zhu Meizhen in the First Special District District Court, seeking to annul the marriage. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Peng Shi held a hearing. Lawyer Qian Yuan and Pan Defan both appeared in court to testify. The other witnesses who were summoned did not appear. According to Lawyer Qian Yuan, he did not know either the plaintiff or the defendant and had never drafted a marriage certificate for them. Judge Peng Shi then handed over the two copies of the marriage certificate submitted by the plaintiff and defendant to Qian for review. Qian stated that although the name seal on the marriage certificate was his, he had never used it since it was engraved and had always kept it in a drawer. If he had been entrusted to handle the marriage certification, he would have used the official seal. Furthermore, he did not attend the wedding ceremony of Chen and others. Therefore, he had not participated in this matter at all. Subsequently, Pan Defan testified that the marriage certificate was actually copied by Ji Wenwei, the secretary of Lawyer Qian Yuan, but the original draft was handwritten by Lawyer Qian. The draft was still kept at Ji's place. Ji feared that Qian would deny his position as secretary, so he specially brought the power of attorney given by Qian to him to prove it. While speaking, he submitted the power of attorney to the court. However, Lawyer Qian ultimately acknowledged that Ji was his secretary but denied drafting the marriage certificate. The next day, the defendant, Zhu Meizhen, testified that she married Chen Yuanzhang and had a wedding banquet at Dahonglou. Chen himself increased or decreased their ages in the marriage certificate. Chen suddenly changed his treatment of her after the marriage, making it difficult to live with him. She had no choice but to return to her mother's house. She only took a set of clothes with her when she left, and the rest of her clothes were still at Chen's house. She was not absconding. Now that Chen was requesting the annulment of the marriage, she was also unwilling to live with him again. However, Chen should pay for her living expenses. Finally, the lawyers of both parties debated with each other. Zhu's lawyer then submitted a counterclaim requesting alimony and requested litigation assistance because Zhu did not have the financial resources to pay the litigation fees. Judge Peng Shi then adjourned the hearing for further review.

Deadline for Stopping the Sale of Old-Style Stamps

Shanghai Postal Administration Notice No. 1193: It has been found that old-version sailboat, agricultural harvest, and round bridge gate ordinary stamps, aviation stamps issued in the 18th year of the Republic (1929), and old-style postage due stamps are limited to be sold until the end of this year. Sales will be stopped after the deadline. After the sales stop, there will be a six-month grace period for general use (i.e., from January 1 to June 30, 1936). During this period, they can still be used for postage. After the deadline, they will be invalid. This notice is hereby issued for public knowledge.

Robberies by Gangs in the French Concession Target Staff and Detectives

Continuous Cases Occurring

All Living in Jiangbei Shantytowns

Recently, with the arrival of the severe winter, gangs of robbers (commonly known as "pig skinners") are occurring every night, especially in remote areas. On both sides of the Sapo Sai Road in the French Concession, from Laoshifu Road south to Kangdi Road, are the ball fields set up by the Chinese Sports Promotion Association, so there are no buildings and few pedestrians at night. The bandits take advantage of this secluded location and lie in ambush in small alleys, waiting for pedestrians or vehicles to pass by, and then come out to rob. Recently, the French police station received reports from victims that many robberies had occurred in that section of the road, so they dispatched Chinese and foreign constables to patrol that section of the road. At about 1:00 AM on the 2nd of this month, French police detective Zhou Ruzhang and constable Gao Hongxuan arrested two Jiangbei robbers, Chen Xiaosi and Yang Xiaobao, near the Huatong Public School set up by the French Public Works Department. They were taken back to the police station. An hour before, the police station had received a report from Qian Yixin, a staff member of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs of the National Government, who lived at No. 1, Hepingfang, Xuehuali Road, that he had been robbed of a coat and dozens of yuan in cash while passing through the area. When questioned, Chen and Yang admitted that they had robbed Qian and had hidden the stolen goods, intending to commit a second robbery. That morning, Chen and Yang were sent to the Second Special Court with a request for a postponement until the 15th pending investigation of other offenses. Unexpectedly, at 11:30 PM the night before, Zhang Ziying, a special detective of the French police station, and Cai Jinzhang, a deputy detective, finished working at the Lujiawan General Police Station and hired rickshaws to go home to bed. Cai's rickshaw was lagging behind because the rickshaw puller was walking slowly, while Zhang's rickshaw was in front. The rickshaw puller ran quickly, turning from Kangdi Road into Sapo Sai Road northward. When he was about to reach the gate of the Huatong Public School, two Jiangbei robbers rushed out of a small alley next to the school's south wall, blocked Zhang's rickshaw, ordered Zhang to get out of the rickshaw, and said to Zhang, "Be nice and help us out." Detective Zhang knew that he was being robbed, so he ordered the rickshaw puller to stop and calmly got out of the rickshaw. He said to the two robbers, "Do you want money or clothes? If you want money, take it yourself. If you want clothes, take them off yourself." The two robbers heard this and replied that it was best to have money, but if there was no money, they would take the clothes. Detective Zhang also said, "If you want money, I have a hundred yuan in cash on me tonight. I'll take it out myself. You are not allowed to move." The two robbers smiled upon hearing this, looking pleased. After Detective Zhang finished speaking, he reached into his pocket as if he was fumbling for money, then pulled out a pistol and aimed it at the chests of the two robbers, shouting, "Hands up! Don't move!" The two robbers were suddenly terrified at the sight of the gun, their bodies trembling, and they did not dare to resist. They raised their hands, standing still like wooden chickens. At this moment, Detective Cai, who was behind him, also arrived in a rickshaw and arrested the two robbers. A search revealed that one of the robbers was carrying an empty flashlight, which was used as a fake gun. When asked for their names, one said his name was Chen Youqing, 22 years old, and the other said his name was Yang Tongguo, nicknamed "Yangtongguan," 20 years old. Both were from Jiangbei and lived in a shantytown in the Shanghai Garrison Camp. They also confessed that they were brothers and relatives of Chen Xiaosi and Yang Xiaobao, who had been arrested earlier. They confessed to committing several robberies, so they were all taken into custody. Yesterday, they were sent to the First Criminal Court of the Second Special Court. Judge Wang Gangxu presided over the interrogation. Police Lawyer Gu Shouxu stated the facts of the case and requested a postponement until the 15th to conduct a detailed investigation, retrieve the stolen goods, and file a lawsuit against the previously arrested robbers Chen Xiaosi and Yang Xiaobao. Detective Zhang Ziying and rickshaw puller testified about the circumstances of the two defendants blocking the road and attempting robbery. The court verified the report, questioned the defendants, and granted the postponement until the 15th to be tried together with Chen Xiaosi and others. The two defendants were returned to custody pending further instructions.

Fire at Dachang New Oil Press

Incomplete Firefighting Equipment

Losses Estimated at Over 100,000 Yuan

Dachang New Oil Press, located at 3 Guangfu Road, Tanjiadu West, Caojiadu, Shanghai West, owned by Zheng Yongbao, specializing in the production of cottonseed oil, was thriving. Yesterday was the factory's regular day off, so work was suspended for the day. Only a few workers were inside the factory repairing and cleaning various machine parts. Unexpectedly, at around 8 a.m., the electric switch in the factory's oil pressing room suddenly broke down when a worker turned it on, immediately igniting a fire. At the same time, the room was covered in oil stains, so the fire quickly spread throughout the building. The workers panicked and fled, rushing to report to the accounting office and grabbing their own fire extinguishers to try to put out the fire, but it was like a drop in the bucket, to no avail. They then urgently reported to the fire department, which dispatched fire trucks to the scene. However, the roads there were rough and difficult for vehicles to travel on, and there were no fire hydrants, so they had to draw water from nearby small creeks. By the time the fire trucks were able to pump water, the fire had already spread to the engine room. The water sprayed by the fire trucks seemed to fuel the flames. After much effort, little progress was made. They then focused on protecting other factory buildings. By around 10 a.m., the fire had been somewhat subdued. As a result, about ten rooms in the oil pressing room and the engine room, as well as machinery, were destroyed by the fire. The losses were estimated to be over 100,000 yuan. It is said that the factory had fire insurance worth 75,000 yuan. After the incident, the Caojiadu Public Security Bureau sent police officers to investigate and summoned the factory owner, Zheng Yongbao, for questioning.

Small Ferry Collision on the Huangpu River Sinks Another

Zhenchang Ferry Hit and Holed

Seventy Workers Rescued Fortunately

Yesterday at around 6 p.m., the Zhenchang small steamer, carrying more than seventy workers from the Huaxing Paper Stack wharf at Gaochang Temple in Nanshi, was heading north, intending to dock in the Hongkou area. When passing the Zhangjiabang water area at the south end of Dongjiadu in Pudong, a small steamer, the Fourth of Qiuxin Factory, was traveling south. The ship was traveling very fast. As the two ships approached each other, neither noticed the other. When they were close and tried to avoid each other, it was too late. The Zhenchang ferry was violently hit by the Qiuxin Factory's small steamer. The hull was holed, and river water rushed in, causing it to sink in an instant. At that time, the workers inside the ship, seeing the dangerous situation, shouted for help. The ship's captain also urgently sounded the siren for help. A great panic arose on the river. It was also during high tide, making the situation critical. The Water Patrol Team of the Municipal Public Security Bureau heard about it and immediately led by Deputy Captain Li Chenghua, along with patrol officers Pan Xutong, Police Chief Yang Bingkui, and more than ten patrolmen, took a patrol boat and rushed to the rescue. They approached the Zhenchang ferry and rescued all seventy-odd workers onto their ship. Only one person was pushed into the water and was immediately rescued. As soon as the workers boarded the patrol boat, the Zhenchang sank. It was a close call, and it was fortunate that there were no fatalities. The captain of the Qiuxin Factory's small steamer, Hou Sanshan, has been detained by Water Patrol Team Leader Li for questioning. The captain of the Zhenchang ferry, Zhu Liangxi, was also taken to the team for questioning.

Da Feng Dyeing and Weaving Factory's Carelessness Last Night

Four Houses Destroyed in Three Quarters of an Hour

At 11:10 p.m. last night, the Da Feng Dyeing and Weaving Factory, located at 90 Guangfu Road, Caojiadu, Shanghai West, was suddenly careless, and a fire quickly spread. The Zhabei fire departments all heard the alarm and drove to the rescue. At that time, the fire was fierce, and it took three quarters of an hour of spraying water to completely extinguish it. According to reports, the factory's work had been completely suspended yesterday morning due to a broken motor. A total of four bungalows were destroyed in the fire, with losses of over a thousand yuan.

New Beijing Sinks Civilian Ship in Ningbo

One Boatman Drowned

The British Taikoo Company's Ningbo liner New Beijing departed from Shanghai on the 7th. On the morning of the 8th, the ship arrived in Zhenhai. It was still 4 a.m. in the early morning. At around 5 a.m., the ship passed Meixu, a place called Aomeng Port. At this time, it was still dark. As it advanced, a civilian ship loaded with bamboo and firewood, traveling from the Cixi countryside to Ningbo, was approaching. At that time, the Xinning-Shaoxing liner was ahead, and the New Beijing liner was behind. The civilian ship was hit by the New Beijing and immediately sank. All the boatmen fell into the water. Fortunately, there were many fishing boats nearby, which came to rescue them. The boat owner, Fang Renlai, and his partner, Wang Afeng, were rescued. Another boatman, Lu Shouren, was not rescued, and his body had drifted away without a trace. The boat owner has reported to the Ningbo Customs and is prepared to negotiate compensation with Taikoo and demand bereavement payments.

Case Cracked from Resolving a Fight

French Concession Promulgates Regulations for the Management of Private Chartered Vehicles

The Shanghai French Concession Municipal Council has recently promulgated new regulations for the management of private chartered vehicles, which are recorded below: (Article 1) Anyone using a chartered vehicle, whether as the owner of the vehicle or as a monthly charterer, must obtain a vehicle license from the Municipal Council, i.e., (Private Chartered Vehicle Permit). (Article 2) This permit shall be issued in the name of the vehicle owner or monthly charterer. The vehicle owner or the monthly charterer shall state in writing that the vehicle is exclusively for the use of himself, his family, or his servants. This permit may also be issued in the name of a society or company. The person in charge of the society or company shall state in writing that the vehicle is exclusively for the use of himself or his staff. In any case, this permit is registered and is only valid within the scope specified in the preceding article. This permit may not be sold, leased, or transferred in any name. If this permit needs to be transferred, it shall be approved in writing by this bureau. (Article 4) The permits issued by this bureau are the same as those issued by the Public Works Department of the Public Concession and can be used interchangeably within the two concessions in a reciprocal relationship. However, all vehicle owners or monthly charterers or societies or companies residing in the French Concession shall apply for permits exclusively from this bureau. (Article 5) The validity period of this permit is one quarter: January 1 is the spring quarter, April 1 is the summer quarter, July 1 is the autumn quarter, and October 1 is the winter quarter. All permits shall be exchanged at the beginning of the quarter. This bureau reserves the right to dispose of permits that have expired. (Article 6) From sunset to sunrise, each chartered vehicle shall be equipped with two bright lights, placed on the left and right sides of the vehicle, emitting white light forward and red light backward. The intensity of the light must be sufficient so that it can be clearly seen at least within twenty-five and eight feet. (Article 7) The permit plate of each chartered vehicle shall be nailed to the vehicle, maintained in good condition, and properly positioned so that the permit number is always clearly visible. (Article 8) No chartered vehicle may be equipped with any alarm bell. (Article 9) Anyone holding a chartered vehicle permit shall comply with all police regulations and shall be responsible for all liabilities caused by the negligence of the vehicle driver. Anyone holding a chartered vehicle permit shall provide the vehicle driver with a copy of the current Municipal Council and Police Department regulations in Chinese and shall explain them in detail to ensure compliance. (Article 10) Anyone holding a chartered vehicle permit shall be responsible for complying with the following regulations: 1. He shall order his vehicle driver to obtain a private chartered vehicle license. 2. If the original vehicle driver is on leave, he shall order his replacement to obtain a private chartered vehicle driver's license. 3. Any change of driver shall be reported to the Vehicle Department within three days. 4. Without special permission from the police station, no more than one vehicle driver may be hired. (Article 11) Anyone holding a chartered vehicle permit shall be responsible for the use of the vehicle and shall not provide the vehicle for public use or rent it out in any name, nor shall he allow anyone to rent it out on his behalf. (Article 12) Anyone holding a chartered vehicle permit shall report any change of address to the Vehicle Department and the Revenue Department within three days. (Article 13) Anyone violating these regulations shall be subject to a fine of between five cents and twenty yuan. Anyone violating the regulations shall immediately present the fine to the head of the police and exchange it for a receipt; otherwise, the police station shall send it to the competent court for investigation. If the violation is serious or if it is a repeated offense, the chartered vehicle permit may be detained or revoked, and further prosecution may still be initiated.

Yi Fangshuo Appeals Rape Case

Yi Fangshuo, the leader of the Fangshuo Jingcheng Troupe from Hangzhou, who sings comic songs and dances at the rooftop garden game field of the New World Department Store and also responds to celebratory hall gatherings, is 43 years old this year and resides at 147, Baxianfang Entrance, Huagene Road, West End of the Eight Immortals Bridge in the French Concession. He was reported to the French Concession Police for raping his under-20-year-old cousin Yi Baozhu, and Yi was arrested. It was also found that Yi had raped his 13-year-old sister-in-law Li Xiaozhen and had bought girls Ye Jinzhu and Yang Lingzhu to train in drama and monitored their freedom of movement. The police department filed a public prosecution with the Second Special District Local Court based on the crimes of obstructing public morals, family, and freedom under the criminal law. After the trial was proposed by Judge Zhang Chaozuo, the rape part was withdrawn at the request of the victims Yi Baozhu and Li Xiaozhen and their guardians Yi Hushi and Li Duofu, and the trial proceeded based on the parts of obstructing family freedom. Yi Fangshuo hired lawyers Sha Xunyi and Hu Jue for defense. As a result of the trial, Yi Fangshuo was sentenced to three years of fixed-term imprisonment for illegally depriving others of their freedom. The part of obstructing public morals was not accepted, and the part of obstructing family was found not guilty. During the appeal period, bail was not allowed, and he was transferred to the detention center to await instructions. The details have been recorded in previous newspapers. It is now known that Yi Fangshuo expressed dissatisfaction with the original judgment and has submitted reasons and a statement to the Second Special Court, requesting that an appeal be filed with the Third Branch Court of the High Court. The Second Special Court has approved it and has sent the entire case file to the Third Branch Court of the High Court for review. It is heard that the High Court will soon summon witnesses and open a court for trial.

Unauthorized Use of Opium to Treat Illness Leads to Death

Ni Ding's Loss of Son Leads to Arrest

In society, there is a common phenomenon of ignorant and foolish people who, when suffering from symptoms such as abdominal pain or diarrhea, often swallow opium ash, believing that opium ash alone can cure all diseases. In reality, this is a great mistake. After the poisonous substance of opium ash enters the abdomen, its nature is extremely violent. If one is not careful and swallows too much, it can lead to death. Such incidents are often heard. Now, Ni Xuegen, a 25-year-old from Wuxi, and his wife, Ni Ding, a 22-year-old, live together at 9 Chongye Lane, Feihong Road, Shanghai North. He works at the Zhang Yichang Copperware Store on Dongyouheng Road in Hongkou, leaving early and returning late, which is common for him. In March of this year, they gave birth to a son named Youhua. The child's physique was quite strong, lively, and lovely. Recently, the infant, who was only ten months old, suddenly suffered from diarrhea. Ni did not seek medical treatment. Ni's wife, Ding, obtained a small amount of opium ash from the neighbor's swallow's nest at around 2 p.m. the day before yesterday and fed it to the infant to swallow. Unexpectedly, the child's face immediately turned red, his expression changed drastically. Ni Ding, seeing this, was horrified and panicked. Only then did she realize that she had mistakenly fed a poisonous substance, and it was too late to regret it. She urgently took the child to Tongren Hospital for treatment, but the poison had been absorbed too deeply, and the treatment was ineffective. His pulse stopped, and his breathing became intermittent until yesterday morning. However, his heart was still warm. Ni Xuegen knew that there was no way to save him, so he took him home, and he soon died. The incident was learned by the Linping Road Police, who sent police officers to arrest and detain Ni Ding. At the same time, they ordered the local guarantor, Ling Renjie, to report to the local court for an autopsy. In the afternoon, Prosecutor Xie Lian and the coroner went to perform the autopsy.

Zhou Weishi's Accusation Case Dismissed

Zhou Weishi, a wealthy merchant from Suzhou living in Shanghai, was accused by Dong Zhihe and other creditors of Gongfa Company in the First Special District Court of Jiangsu and Shanghai, with lawyers Dong Yu and others hired. They requested confirmation that Zhou was a shareholder of Gongfa Company. The physical evidence they presented was the name of Zhou Weishi in the shareholder register of Gongfa Company, noting that he held one share. They also cited Yuan Ludeng and Ye Shantao, directors of Gongfa Company, as proof that they had heard Huang Chuqiu say that Zhou was a director of the company. Zhou also hired lawyer Zhu Sifu to file a defense, stating that the evidence presented by the plaintiff was insufficient to prove that the Zhou Weishi in the shareholder register was Zhou Weishi, his client. The testimony of witnesses Yuan and Ye was hearsay and could not be used as evidence according to the precedent of the Daliyuan. After the debate concluded, Judge Peng Shi of the Fourteenth Civil Court of the First Special Court announced the judgment yesterday afternoon: The plaintiff's lawsuit was dismissed, and the litigation costs were borne by the plaintiff.

Central Bank Inspection Report

Two Hundred and Twentieth

The Central Bank's two hundred and twentieth inspection report on the issue reserve states: In accordance with Article 15 of the Central Bank Ordinance, this committee is responsible for inspecting the reserve fund for the exchange vouchers issued by this bank. The two hundred and twentieth inspection was held at the Issuing Bureau of this bank on January 10, 1935. The results of the inspection are hereby made public as follows: (A) Total amount of exchange vouchers issued: silver dollars 89,034,250, including: silver dollar vouchers 82,784,886, subsidiary currency vouchers 6,249,364. Total amount of exchange voucher reserve: silver dollars 89,034,250, including: cash reserve silver dollars 70,516,250. The cash reserve is composed of 65,879,398 stored in the bank's issuing vault, 2,747,733 stored in branch banks, and 1,889,119 stored in correspondent banks. Guarantee reserve converted to silver dollars 18,518,000. (B) Total amount of Customs Gold Unit exchange vouchers issued: 373,324.7 Customs Gold Units. Total amount of Customs Gold Unit exchange voucher reserve: 373,324.7 Customs Gold Units. The reserve includes 7,351 taels, 9 mace, and 5 fen of silver bullion, calculated at a fixed price of 50.779 to equal 373,324.7 Customs Gold Units. According to Article 2 of the Central Bank Exchange Voucher Regulations, the cash reserve is 60% and the guarantee reserve is 40%. The inspection results show that the cash exceeds 60% and the guarantee is less than 40%, which is in compliance with the regulations. This report is submitted on January 11, 1935, by Li Fusun, Chairman of the Board of Supervisors of the Central Bank, and Supervisors Xie Mingxun, Bei Songsun, Qin Runqing, Yu Qiaqing, Lin Kanghou, and Xu Jili.

Spring and Autumn

Little West Heaven

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Seven: Hearing Words, She Hides Her Tears and Sells Herself into Hardship, Carefully Secretly Seeks to Rely on Him with Ardent Affection.

These words caused Wang Beihai to blush. Because his possessions were not easily acquired, he shouldn't give them away so readily. Seeing his red face, Cheng Zhiqian couldn't help but think that his words had been too direct, so he smiled at Aunt Hu and said, "Even so, you can't disregard people's kindness. But it's unreasonable to just accept someone's empty kindness. Now, let me mediate. Tomorrow morning, Aunt Hu can come to my place to take three or four catties of flour. This flour will be considered a gift from Mr. Wang." Aunt Hu laughed, "Oh! Mr. Cheng's explanation makes everything clear, why do you still need to buy flour for me?" Wang Beihai said, "That's Mr. Cheng's kindness, you can't dismiss it." Yueying looked from Zhiqian's face to Beihai's face, nodded slightly, and whispered, "We thank you first." Aunt Hu was even more beaming with joy, thanking them repeatedly. That Miss Yueying didn't feel much receiving the two dollars from Cheng Zhiqian. Only Wang Beihai, in such difficult circumstances, was willing to share half of his flour, which was truly touching. Therefore, thanking them as she walked out, her eyes were still fixed on Wang Beihai. The meaning seemed to be saying, "Although I can't say anything, I'm very grateful to you in my heart." Because she was thinking this way, she first supported the back of the chair, then the corner of the table, and then the half-open door. It was as if something had suddenly gone wrong with her legs, making it difficult for her to walk. As she reached the door, Aunt Hu hurried forward and pulled her sleeve, saying, "Let's go, don't tear the borrowed clothes. Return them quickly." It was the truth, a young and self-conscious girl, in front of a young male student, this embarrassment was no less than Jia Duocai's face-to-face criticism of her appearance. She didn't say anything more and followed Aunt Hu out. (110)

Wang Renqiu's Commentary on "Investiture of the Gods"

— Yanqiao

Wang Renqiu's Xiangqilou Diary contains discussions about "Investiture of the Gods," which are recorded below.

" 'Investiture of the Gods' was originally intended to be like 'Water Margin' and 'Journey to the West,' and it also borrows from 'Romance of the Three Kingdoms.' Its writing is disorderly and dates back to after the Jiajing era of the Ming Dynasty. However, the common people widely believe in it, even to the point of altering the titles of gods. Even today, the Four Heavenly Kings, the Hum-Ha Gods, the God of Wealth, and the God of Smallpox all originate from it, and it has become an unchangeable classic among the common people. When I was a child, I liked its mention of the Taiji Diagram causing the disaster of being burned to death, which was probably meant to satirize the Ming Emperor Taizong's killing of Fang Xiaoru and other gentlemen. And its mention of pigs and dogs assisting Bai Zhu Zongrong was meant to satirize Li Jinglong and other generals, believing that each had its target. However, its text has expanded into hundreds of thousands of characters, and it must have some intention to be able to elaborate. And Wen Zhong is also meant to be like Zhang Jiangling, who was arrogant without learning. Its mention of the "Withered Ring" clearly refers to the Tingji incident. People of the Ming Dynasty liked to write about legends and romances, and this one is particularly humorous, strange, and unfair, with many accusations. In general, it takes wealth and lust as warnings, so it particularly values Zhao Gongming and his sister. Wealth is the brother and lust is the sister, and there can be no lust without wealth. Placing them among the Ten Absolutes means that they have killed countless lives, especially in middle age, when they are still involved in wealth and lust. When the Ten Absolutes are broken, the immortals are killed, and when the Ten Thousand Immortals are defeated, they are like monkeys wearing hats. This means that from commoners to emperors, they cannot be trapped in the Soul-Reaping Formation by the Taiji Diagram. Therefore, they must use the Taiji Diagram to easily disregard human life. It is not allowed for the Crown Prince to enter the Taiji Diagram, which is what those who hate the times and resent vulgarity do. The main point is that the wise and intelligent all help the rebels, and the slanderous and evil all become gods. Only birds and beasts can communicate with heaven, and it is extremely disgusted with the words of the scholars of the Song Dynasty. It is suspected to be the work of Li Zhuowu. In the past, I suspected that it contained the theory of Jindan medical prescriptions and wanted to comment on it, but now I know that it is still a pedantic scholar, so I mark its intention in this way. As for its divine names, they probably have other sources and did not originate from this, so there is nothing to examine."

Who is the author of "Investiture of the Gods"? Modern people have already investigated it. Sun Kaidi's "Catalog of Chinese Popular Novels," Volume 5, Section B of Ming and Qing Novels, records: "'Investiture of the Gods,' one hundred chapters, written by Xu Zhonglin of the Ming Dynasty. (Note: According to the Ming edition in two volumes, titled Zhonglin, a native of Yingtian Prefecture, Nanjing, with an unknown name and the pseudonym Zhongshan Yisou. A book is stored in the Cabinet Library of Japan, a Ming edition. This is its crowning achievement."

Wang Renqiu's words are inevitably far-fetched. The story of King Wu's conquest of Zhou already existed in the Song Dynasty, and Xu only expanded and elaborated on it, and it may not have the intention of satirizing politics. Scholars like to interpret deeply and intricately, and they are mostly like this. Renqiu once wanted to comment on it, but fortunately he didn't, otherwise it would only be like a lecture with a high head, and he may not have the literary insight of Jin Shengtan.

Hard Struggle in Recession

— 19

Then it seemed there was a slight sense of clearing, so I took advantage of the gap to go out on the street for a walk to buy some things. The main street was strangely lively. Men and women were jostling each other, and traffic was endless. Music was audible everywhere. In front of the shops, colorful sheds were erected, painted with pictures such as "Zhao Zilong Alone Rescuing the Young Lord" and "Liu Xuande Thrice Visiting the Thatched Cottage," attracting people to look up and point fingers as they commented. At first glance, who could say that this was not a scene of prosperity?

But some shops, because they couldn't afford to erect colorful sheds or hire musicians, had to build high platforms in front of their doors, with two people standing there making faces, forcing their throats to shout. "Luzon hats, buy one for two dimes, it's nice to wear on a cold day." They shouted like this in turn, forcing their throats to shout like this, and they were already hoarse, but the audience in front of the platform only raised their heads, opened their mouths, and stared blankly at the faces and the Luzon hats. Ah! What is this scene?

Walking further, I saw two shoe shops, both with a one-bay storefront, and they were next to each other. In front of one shop, a colorful shed was erected, which was strangely eye-catching. Probably because the shop had just finished repairs, there were couplets on both sides of the colorful shed. The couplet characters were red and green, and the words were, "Now that the construction is successful, the opening is celebrated as usual." On the sidewalk in front of the door, there was also a Qingyin stage, and even pedestrians couldn't pass through. In front of the other shop, it was deserted, with only a wooden sign hanging high. On the red paper, the five words "Grand Sale in This Shop" were written in large characters; next to it, there was a line of sloppy characters, which read: "The Qingyin colorful shed is a waste of money, it's originally cheating people for food!"

Seeing this, I couldn't help but be stunned. Competition among peers to grab business is common in large cities and is not surprising; but if this phenomenon also exists in the interior, then how can it only be described as "recession"? The six words "Originally cheating people for food" are a kind of wail issued after the exhaustion of plans, and at the same time, it also carries a hint of anger. Alas, they are struggling hard!

Shanghai-Guangdong Sightseeing Flight Encountered Fog (Continued)

— Qian Hua

At nine o'clock sharp, the plane landed in Wenzhou. Representatives from local agencies came to welcome us and invited them to try out the new plane. Six people formed a group, and each flight lasted eight minutes, for a total of five flights. The representatives' wives and daughters were also dressed up in the crowd. During this free time, we crossed the river and took rickshaws to tour the city. At eleven o'clock, we flew directly from Wenzhou to Fuzhou again, and it was expected to arrive at half past twelve. Flying until eleven forty, we saw from afar that the white clouds on the tops of the mountains suddenly thickened. In an instant, the white clouds descended to the mountainside, and the mountainside became blurred. Several white clouds flew head-on towards the plane, becoming more and more numerous, and finally the surroundings were all white, and it was impossible to tell whether the bottom was sea or mountain, and it was even impossible to tell the direction of east, west, north, and south. My heart suddenly began to beat faster, and everyone's faces involuntarily showed panic. At the same time, the radio received news that the plane flying north from Guangzhou had also encountered fog and turned back. Mr. Dai passed the telegram to us for viewing and said calmly, "Let's go back to Wenzhou for dinner first." We looked at each other without saying a word, and the pilot immediately steered the plane to turn around and fly back. The white clouds surrounding us gradually thinned, and twenty minutes later, we completely broke out of the heavy fog and returned to clear mountains and rivers.

We returned to Wenzhou at half past twelve. Our group still had a glimmer of hope, which was to wait for the weather report from Fuzhou. If the heavy fog receded, we could continue flying. Waiting until one o'clock in the afternoon, the weather report from Fuzhou came, but the result was that the situation was getting worse. So, with a disappointed look, we boarded the plane silently and returned to Shanghai.

Afterwards, according to the pilot Mr. Fang Si, today's fog was still light fog, because the number of white clouds was not large, and there were many gaps in the middle, so we could still see the scenery on the ground clearly. We could have risked rushing through and flying to Fuzhou, but for the sake of caution, we had to turn back. He also said that the plane is most afraid of fog, followed by storms. China's flight equipment is very incomplete. If there were coastal radio stations that reported the appropriate flight angles at any time during heavy fog, then blind flying would also be possible, and it would be very safe. (End)

Walking in the Garden at Dawn

— Geng Bai

The neighbor's rooster breaks the dream, the sound of the horn is mournful, I get up and walk around the dwelling, leaning on the green moss. The thin dusk is the place of morning air, and the cold flowers send out a faint fragrance from time to time. I am the first to worry and rejoice for the world, and the rise and fall of the masses are all incompetent. I still have some wisdom left to explore in my bag, and I will try to fly and control the wind and thunder!

Winter at Zǐlóu

— Lín Gēngbái

Winter has quietly entered my small Zǐlóu. Sitting alone at my desk, pen in hand, paper spread out, I gaze out the window, and a boundless number of misanthropic emotions ignite the remnants of my wounded heart. I want to yearn for the future, but I cannot help but shatter reality, and even more so, I cannot forget the past. The mission of transforming the new society has liberated me from the pain of love and the entanglements of life, giving me a fresh strength. What a comfort that should be?

But adorable young women constantly flicker in my eyes. I want to close them, but the light in the darkness won't allow me, because even with my eyes shut, there always seems to be an inseparable illusion lingering in my mind. The circles within my eyelids are always inseparable from this hazy shadow. What should I do? Am I still unable to forget the past? I doubt it.

Many fallen leaves in the corner of the wall gradually transition from withered green to scorched yellow. This symbolizes the cold and ruthless winter, extending its authority, making people feel the transience of life, along with the fading of everything. At the same time, within the scarlet embroidered curtains, there will be ripples of faint sunlight, making people feel beautiful and bright. Doesn't this tell people that even though winter has covered the earth, the warmth is brewing the rebirth of the coming year? The mission of transforming the new society, the flickering adorable young women, which is the epitome of spring? Conflicting and contradictory fantasies comfort me, but also confuse me even more.

Without pain, joy cannot be produced; without conflict, order cannot be achieved; without contradiction, unity cannot be discovered. Then perhaps this confusion is the starting point of my final comfort? This first, second, third, fourth, and so on, so many confusions, in the final act, will be like floating clouds, highlighting the azure sky.

I am excited. I'm calculating the schedule. Today is Friday, tomorrow is Saturday, and the day after tomorrow is Sunday. Starting next week, no matter how lazy and annoyed I am, I must change my life, prepare for the things that need to be done, and follow the path that should be taken. Every day, every moment, every second, I should strictly discipline myself, because I understand my personality well: it needs stimulation and encouragement. In that moment of realization, the shadow of the adorable young woman flickers again.

The intellectual class will ultimately maintain its standard of living. This is the modern capitalist society, shaping their consciousness and emotions. No one is an exception, unless there is a fundamental transformation of the world's economic system. I pity the gentlemen who do not even recognize this and simply clamor for the inherent culture, desperately rushing towards the dead end of regression. They cannot imagine that the current Chinese society, all of life, has completely changed, at least in urban society. This is clearly influenced by the international economic system. Therefore, in the context of the general reflection of life in China, during the transition from China's agricultural economy to an industrial economy, the only way to transform a new society is to create a unique new economic system. Otherwise, we would have to revert to the old life and the economic system before material civilization invaded China, to assimilate society and maintain consistency. But who can deny that this is comical? When I think of transforming the new society, I cannot help but muster the courage to move forward fearlessly.

Before my eyes is still winter after all. I look forward to spring. I hide in a corner of the small Zǐlóu, shouting that spring is coming soon, but how should I spend this winter? I cannot just shout aimlessly. For example, to plant a tree, one must also sow the seeds, diligently irrigate them, so that they sprout, so that in the spring, they can grow from sprouts into branches and leaves, and from branches and leaves, bloom with buds. I think this is funny. If I were a tree, the new life in my fantasy would be this last, brilliant flower. But the flower not only needs irrigation, it also needs the nourishment of rain and dew and the bathing of sunlight. My own efforts towards the future are nothing more than the function of irrigation. Young woman! You must bestow rain and dew and sunlight, so that this thriving tree has a day to bloom the flower of this new society, and then the coldness before my eyes will naturally be taken away by the warm spring. After writing this little essay, it seems that the god of hope is beckoning. I forgot the coldness, I forgot all the coldness.

Records of Lingering Fragrance

— Originally Written by Princess Deling of the Qing Dynasty, Translated by Qin Shouou

"After the emperors have rested and relaxed in this palace, their spirits are completely replenished, and their attendants simultaneously prepare all the necessary bows and horses. Then, he stands up, tidies his clothes, and quickly mounts his horse, galloping into the open field. At this time, those in charge of tigers and leopards have received their cue and open the wooden cages, letting the wild beasts rush out. At the same time, many people around shout loudly or use long spears and halberds to provoke them, ensuring they are startled or enraged. These wild beasts will first flee desperately into the forest. Once they enter the forest, those people, each wearing brightly colored hunting clothes and carrying complete weapons, will separate and drive them out of the forest. However, they do not directly engage with the wild beasts, but instead throw lit firecrackers into the forest, disturbing the beasts with loud noises, preventing them from staying in the forest. The beasts then bravely jump out of the forest, right in front of where the emperor is waiting. In this way, three arrows are continuously shot from the emperor's bow. If all three arrows hit their mark, the wild beast is destined to die, and the emperor's archery skills can earn him the reputation of being skilled! If only one or two of the three arrows hit, it is still considered good, because arrows fired from stronger bows can often kill a tiger or leopard with just one arrow. However, there are also times when one, two, or even three arrows fail to kill the beast. In that case, the emperor must disregard all danger, draw his sword, and rush forward, making sure to kill it before he can stop." (220)

Ten Current Educational Personnel are Examined and Sent from Various Provinces

And the Third Scholarship Examination is Held

(Northeast News Agency, Changchun) The puppet Ministry of Education has recently intensified its efforts to promote puppet-style slave education. It has also scheduled the third scholarship selection examination to be held on December 10th, 11th, 12th, and 13th of last year. Those who pass will be sent to Japanese universities, specialized schools, or higher middle schools to study, starting from April of this year. The key points of the third scholarship student selection examination are listed below: (1) Number of admissions: Several students for Japanese high schools, specialized schools, and universities; several students for secondary schools; several students for the "Manzhou" Medical University, Lushun Engineering University, and South Manchuria Industrial Specialized School within "the country." (2) Technical examination qualifications: Applicants who wish to enter Japanese or "domestic" higher specialized schools and universities should have a higher secondary school graduation qualification or equivalent academic ability. (3) Application dates: From November 10th to November 30th. Two photos. The paper for the above documents must be obtained from the Education Department of the applicant's province of origin, or the Education Department of the special zone, the Education Section of the special municipality, the Japanese embassy, or the "Ministry of Education." The submitted documents and examination fee will not be returned regardless of admission. No receipts will be issued for the examination fee, but an examination certificate will be issued in its place. (5) Examination dates: Between December 10th, 11th, 12th, and 13th of last year. (6) Examination subjects: 1. Academic examination: Chinese interpretation, Chinese composition, mathematics, Japanese, English, 2. Physical examination, 3. Oral examination. (7) Examination locations: The Education Department of "Feng Province" and the Education Department of the Jilin, Heilongjiang, Rehe, and Beiman Special Zone Public Offices, the "Xinjing" Special Municipal Government, and the Japanese embassy. (8) Announcement date: After January 10th of the second year (i.e., the second year of the puppet Kangde). (9) Monthly allowance: 1. 60 yuan for universities in Tokyo, Osaka, Kyoto, Yokohama, and Kobe, 50 yuan for specialized schools and specialized departments, 45 yuan for higher schools, university preparatory courses, preparatory departments, and specially established higher courses, 40 yuan for specially established preparatory courses, 25 yuan for secondary schools. 2.
