Funding for National Vocational Schools and Above

The Ministry of Education has compiled statistics on the funding for national vocational schools and above for the 21st year. The main points are recorded separately below:

(1) The total funding for national universities in the 21st year was 22,682,910 yuan, of which 13,002,747 yuan was for 13 national universities (Sun Yat-sen University had the most at over 2 million yuan, Central University had over 1.7 million yuan, Beiping had 1.55 million yuan, Tsinghua had 1.23 million yuan, and the remainder ranged from Wuhan's 960,000 to Sichuan's 310,000 yuan). 2,400,244 yuan was for 9 provincial universities (Guangxi, Henan, and Donglu each had over 400,000 yuan, and Northeast Jiaotong University had only 39,000 yuan). 7,279,919 yuan was for 19 private universities (Yanjing had the most at over 1 million yuan, Lingnan had 780,000 yuan, Qilu had 540,000 yuan, Jinling had 460,000 yuan, 7 schools had over 300,000 yuan, 6 schools had over 200,000 yuan, and Datong had the least at 91,000 yuan).

(2) The total funding for national independent colleges was 8,633,342 yuan, of which 965,016 yuan was for 5 national colleges (Beiyang Institute of Technology had 323,655 yuan, and Guangdong College of Law had only 85,512 yuan). 1,185,304 yuan was for 11 provincial colleges (Hebei Institute of Technology had 207,306 yuan, Jiangsu Education College had over 190,000 yuan, 4 colleges had below 150,000 yuan, and 4 colleges had between 45,000 and 93,000 yuan). 6,553,022 yuan was for 19 private colleges (Xiehe had the most at over 3,995,000 yuan, Fujian Xiehe had 400,000 yuan, Zhijiang College of Arts and Sciences had over 210,000 yuan, 12 colleges had between 100,000 and 180,000 yuan, and 4 colleges had between 36,000 and 70,000 yuan).

(3) The total funding for national vocational schools was 1,887,569 yuan, of which 183,442 yuan was for 2 national schools, 430,675 yuan was for 5 ministry-run schools, 823,017 yuan was for 12 provincial schools, and 450,435 yuan was for 8 private schools.

(4) The total funding for the above three types of schools, vocational schools, independent colleges, and universities, was 33,203,821 yuan, of which teachers' salaries accounted for 11,144,339 yuan, staff salaries accounted for 3,632,653 yuan, workers' wages accounted for 170,575 yuan, equipment expenses accounted for 6,216,559 yuan, office expenses accounted for 3,259,999 yuan, special expenses accounted for 221,496 yuan, and expenses for affiliated institutions accounted for 2,137,43 yuan.

Three Organizations in Beijing Hold an Exhibition of the German Poet Schiller

Zhu Jia驊 reports on the significance of the event

The preparatory office of the Central Library and the German-Austrian-Swiss Alumni Association and the Sino-German Cultural Association held the opening ceremony of the German poet Schiller exhibition at the Overseas Chinese Reception Center at 3 p.m. on the 10th. Zhu Jia骅, Wang Shijie, the secretary of the German Embassy in China, Fang Deshi, Jiang Fuyi, the director of the preparatory office of the National Central Library, and nearly 100 Chinese and German guests attended. Zhu Jia骅 presided over the meeting and reported on the process and significance of initiating the exhibition. Wang Shijie then gave a speech, and finally Fang Deshi delivered a speech on behalf of the German Ambassador. The meeting adjourned around 4 p.m. The exhibition will be open to the public for three days starting from the 11th.

Minister of Communications Zhu Jia骅 delivered an opening speech at the Schiller exhibition, stating briefly: "It is a great honor to represent the German-Austrian-Swiss Alumni Association to hold the opening ceremony of the Schiller exhibition today. The materials for the exhibition were collected by the Sino-German Cultural Association from the German side and the Peking University Library. The materials are divided into five major parts: 1. Schiller's life, 2. Works, 3. Portraits, 4. Schiller as a playwright, 5. Works about Schiller and Chinese translations. Schiller was a fighter, not fighting for his personal life, not only fighting for the German people, but fighting for the freedom of all mankind. Schiller is now closer to us than any other German writer. In terms of art, Schiller is also very similar to the Chinese stage. His views on drama coincide with those of our country's playwrights. Today's exhibition is also intended to let us know the life and art of this great German writer. Moreover, today's exhibition also has a more universal significance for China and Germany. China and Germany have had ideological relations since the 17th century. The works produced by the exchange of ideas are too numerous to mention. China and Germany have a relationship that is 400 years deep. It is our duty to maintain this friendship. The Schiller exhibition held today is also based on this idea to promote cultural exchange between China and Germany for the benefit of the people of both countries who share the same fate."

The Chinese Painting Society Holds Its Third General Meeting

More Than 100 Members Attended a Dinner and Photo Session at Guanshengyuan

Wang Yiting, Chen Shuren, and others were re-elected as executive and supervisory committee members

The Chinese Painting Society is the only organization jointly initiated by Chinese calligraphers and painters to promote China's inherent art and culture. Since it was approved by the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau in the autumn of the 22nd year and filed with the Nanjing Ministry of Education, it has made great efforts to promote its affairs. In addition to holding calligraphy and painting exhibitions at home and abroad to arouse the awareness and interest of people at home and abroad in China's art, it also publishes a picture monthly, which is entirely aimed at promoting art and culture. Yesterday was the expiration of the term of the second executive and supervisory committee members of the society. The general meeting of members was held at the society on Weihaiwei Road. More than 100 members from this city and other places attended. At 6 p.m., a dinner and photo session was also held at Guanshengyuan on Nanjing Road, which was an unprecedented event in the Chinese calligraphy and painting circles. The conference situation is recorded below:

Attending Members: The members from this city who attended included He Tianjian, Zhang Yuguang, Yu Jingzhi, Chen Ziheng, Jiang Yinan, Jiang Yanan and her daughter, Shen Yizhai, Ma Qizhou, Qian Shoutie, Wu Zhongxi, Wu Qingxia and her daughter, Ding Nianxian, Wu Jiaxing, Diao Shilin, Wang Yiting, Dai Yunqi, Ying Yeping, Zhu Rongzhuang, Ma Gongyu, Li Qishi, Luo Junti, Xu Muru, Yao Mocun, Sun Xueni, Chen Jinghong, Lu Danlin, Chen Xiaodie, Zheng Wuchang, Gu Boda, Shi Chongpeng, and others, totaling over 100 people. Members from other cities, such as Deng Qingcheng, also attended from afar, which was especially commendable.

Conference Situation: The meeting opened at 2 p.m., presided over by He Tianjian, with Ding Nianxian as the recorder. (A) Reporting Items: (1) The work situation of the second executive and supervisory committee, (2) The third issue of the Chinese Painting Monthly will be published within days, (3) The newly compiled membership directory is already in printing, (4) The economic part will be reported in writing. (B) Resolutions: (1) Amend the articles of association, (2) Determine the outline of the work plan for the third executive and supervisory committee, (3) Reappoint Li Qishi as the general secretary of the society, (4) Organize a travel group.

Re-election Results: Sun Xueni, He Tianjian, Zhang Yuguang, Qian Shoutie, Zheng Wuchang, Xie Gongzhan, Chen Xiaodie, Ma Qizhou, Lu Danlin, and others were elected as executive committee members. Zhang Daqian, Wang Yachen, Wang Shizi, Shen Yizhai, Ding Nianxian, Ma Gongyu, and others were elected as alternate committee members. Wang Yiting, Huang Binhong, Chen Shuren, Zhang Shanzi, Jing Henggu, and others were elected as supervisors. Shang Shengbo, Xiong Songzhu, Wang Zhongshan, Li Zukui, and others were elected as alternate supervisors.

The County Education Bureau Examines the Academic Performance of Students in Various Primary Schools

The Shanghai County Education Bureau conducts examinations of the academic performance of students in various primary schools every semester to promote improvements in teaching by teachers. The bureau sent personnel to various districts at the beginning of this month to conduct examinations on sixth-grade natural science and fifth-grade arithmetic. All the test papers from each school have been graded, and the results have been compiled. Among the sixth-grade students tested, there were 255 students, with Sanlin being the best. Among the fifth-grade students tested, there were 394 students, with Minhang Central being the best. Among the fourth-grade students tested, there were 682 students, with Minhang Central being the best among complete primary schools and Yucai being the best among junior primary schools. Statistical results for each item have been distributed to various primary schools for their reference.

Committee Members for the Custody of Private Submissions for the London Exhibition of Chinese Art

The members of the Preparatory Committee and Specialized Committee, Honorary Secretaries, and Secretaries of the London International Exhibition of Chinese Art have been gradually published in newspapers. It is reported that in addition to the 180 bronze ware items and over 300 calligraphy, paintings, and porcelain items already selected by the Palace Museum, the libraries of Peking University, Yenching University, Shandong, Henan, and Anhui provinces, as well as the Central Wu Research Institute, Nanjing Antiquities Preservation Institute, and the History Museum, also have submissions. In addition, there are private collectors who are willing to send their cherished ancient and precious calligraphy, paintings, porcelain, and other items for display. Those that meet the standards after review will also be shipped out for exhibition. Regarding the custody of these private submissions, the Preparatory Committee has organized a Private Submissions Custody Committee. Yesterday, letters were sent to invite Wang Yunwu, Cai Yuanpei, Ye Gongchuo, Cheng Linsheng, and Qian Yongming to serve as Private Submissions Custody Committee members, and Wang Yunwu was also invited to serve as the Chief Custody Committee Member. In addition to inviting Pan Gongzhan, Lei Zhen, Li Shengwu, and Hang Liwu to serve as Honorary Secretaries, the committee also added He Deji of the Shanghai Municipal Council as an Honorary Secretary to assist with all matters related to the pre-exhibition to be held in Shanghai in March and the establishment of an office in Shanghai.

Overseas Chinese Li Pei Returns to China to Investigate Education

Visits various schools in the city for several days

Yesterday evening, he went to Beijing to pay respects to the Minister of Education for instructions

Li Pei, the principal of the Chinese School of Yasuhan Peizhong in Sumatra, believes that the educational facilities for overseas Chinese should be in line with the education of the home country. He has returned to China to investigate the current state of education in China to serve as a reference for running education for overseas Chinese. Since arriving in Shanghai, Mr. Li has visited universities and social education institutions to observe and learn. He also went to Beijing last night to pay respects to Minister of Education Wang Shijie, to ask for instructions on the guidelines for running education for overseas Chinese. He also plans to visit major cities to investigate education.

Universal Chinese Students' Association Hires Professors

News from the Universal Chinese Students' Association at 191 Carter Road, Shanghai, states that the association has been entrusted by a certain university in another province to seek one professor each for Chinese Literature and Education, and for Mathematics, Physics, and Civil Engineering. The Chinese Literature professor should be a graduate of a domestic or foreign university, have special achievements in Chinese literature (preferably with published works), and have teaching experience. The professor will be responsible for courses such as Logic, Phonology, History of Chinese Philosophy, Poetry and Lyrics, Exegesis, and Textual Research for the first, second, and third grades, and must prepare lecture notes. The Education professor should be a graduate of an American or British university with a degree, have definite research in education, and have teaching experience. The professor will be responsible for courses such as Vocational Education, Comparative Education, Social Education, Intelligence Testing, Educational Psychology, Educational Thought, Educational Administration, and History of Education. Textbooks in both Chinese and English will be used, and lecture notes must be prepared if suitable textbooks are unavailable. The Mathematics, Physics, and Civil Engineering professor should be a graduate of an American or British university with a degree, have special research in mathematics and physics, and have teaching experience. The professor will be responsible for courses such as Advanced Physics and Electricity.

The monthly salary for each of the above three professorships is 200 yuan in national currency, calculated on the basis of twelve months per year. The maximum teaching time per week is 18 hours, with a minimum of 15 hours. Teaching will be conducted in Mandarin. A travel allowance of 200 yuan in national currency will be provided. In addition, a certain institution in another province needs to hire one Hydraulic Engineering Technician and one Statistician. Candidates should be graduates of domestic or foreign universities with definite research and experience in the above-mentioned work. The monthly salary is 250 yuan. Those who are willing to apply can send a detailed resume to the association at 191 Carter Road.

Recent News from the Nian Er Society in Western Shanghai

The Nian Er Society in Western Shanghai, which aims to promote domestic goods, practice social frugality, strive for social production and development, promote the national economy, improve the lives of the people, and work together for the revival of the Chinese nation, has been established for a year since last spring. In the past year, the work done, such as promoting domestic goods, improving native cloth, and creating popular education, has been well-known. Recently, in order to help solve the problem of education funding, it has also piloted a consumer aid society, aiming to promote local products from various places and introduce daily necessities, and allocate all profits for the popularization of civil education near the society. The grand opening is scheduled for February of this year. In addition, the society's educational work has now been entirely moved to Zhongshan Village, where two cooperatives, a rickshaw pulling cooperative and a planting cooperative, have been established to promote civil education. The original textile cooperative, because its members all reside in the Daxia Civil Education Experimental Zone, was transferred to the Jinjia Lane Rural Nian Er Society in the Daxia Civil Education Zone last autumn. The various native cloths produced are still sold by the Nian Er Society in Western Shanghai, and it is said that sales are very prosperous.

Publication of "Stories of Chinese Literature and Art"

Co-edited by Xu Zhengji and Sun Yucai

Mr. Xu Zhengji and Mr. Sun Yucai, who have served in the education sector in this city for many years, have written extensively. Their newly compiled book "Stories of Chinese Literature and Art" has a total length of over 50,000 words. The content is rich, the materials are valuable, and the selection criteria are: (1) developing thought, (2) having literary meaning, (3) being interesting without involving fantasy, and (4) not violating the spirit of the times. Wu Yanyin, an expert in elementary education, wrote in the preface: "I am willing to be the introducer of this book. I hope that elementary and middle school teachers will designate this book as extracurricular reading material for elementary and middle school students, and try to bring out the advantages of this book as much as possible." It is said that the book is published by Dahua Bookstore. The World Bookstore and major bookstores in this city are selling it. It is divided into two volumes, with a price of two jiao per volume.

Shenbao Radio Weekly

How to Make a Straight-Line Dial

— Wang Shengshi

Many radios in Europe now use straight-line dials. The style is novel and beautiful, but the structure is very simple. Below is a method of imitating it. The materials are very cheap. Just a little effort is needed to make it.

First, prepare a small piece of cardboard, a small piece of five-hao-thick wood, and two sections of glass tubes (or bamboo pen tubes) with a diameter of about eight hao and a length of about one centimeter, and one leather shoelace. After preparing the materials, follow the method below.

This method can be used for all kinds of radios, but for the sake of simplicity, let's assume it's a two-board DC machine. The original capacitors are mostly installed in the middle of the panel. Now we need to modify it first. Cut off a piece of wood measuring six centimeters high and three centimeters wide and nail it to the middle of the base plate, one centimeter away from the panel. Drill a hole four centimeters high in the middle of this small piece of wood, and also drill a hole in the same position on the panel. Then, if the capacitor is fixed on the small board, its rotating shaft can extend out of the panel.

Draw another circle with a diameter of six centimeters on the prepared board, and carefully saw it off with a copper wire saw. Smooth the edges with a rasp. Drill a hole in the center, about six hao in diameter, slightly smaller than the diameter of the capacitor's rotating shaft. Then cut two cardboard pieces into circles with a diameter of seven centimeters, and cut a large hole in the middle. Glue them to both sides of the wooden board, so that five hao is exposed all around. (Figure 2)

Looking at (Figure 3), it is the general outline of the dial. Draw the dimensions on the panel according to the diagram. Hole C is where the capacitor's rotating shaft is placed. The dotted line is the small wooden board. The square block with the black line needs to be cut away. This step must be paid attention to, because it is related to the overall aesthetics. Nail two small tacks at points A and B on the back of the panel, and put two small sections of glass tube (or bamboo pen tube) on the tacks, which can rotate freely, but cannot slide out because they are blocked by the tack heads. At this time, the capacitor can be installed. First, insert the rotating shaft into the hole of the small wooden board from the back, then take the round wooden board and forcefully put it on the shaft, and then fix the capacitor on the small wooden board. Part of the shaft extends out of the panel, as shown in (Figure 4), and a small knob can be used to fix it on it. The round wooden board must be tightly fitted on the shaft, and cannot be allowed to slide.

Then, use a leather shoelace about four hao wide, as shown in Figure 3, tightly wrapped around the round wooden board, and then routed from A and B to the top. Pull the two ends of the belt tight, and cut a small copper piece into the shape of (Figure 5), fold it along the dotted line, put it on the joint of the belt, clamp it with pliers, and cut off the end of the belt. This belt is very firmly connected. Use another piece of 26-gauge copper wire two centimeters long, flatten one end, and solder the other end to the copper piece at the joint to make a pointer. At this time, when the capacitor is rotated, the pointer moves in the square hole.

Then take a business card-sized piece of white paper, cut it into the size shown in Figure 6, fold it along the dotted line, and glue it to the back of the square hole on the panel, as shown in the dotted line in Figure 3. Many straight lines can be drawn on this white paper to indicate the frequency of the radio stations.

First, make the fixed and moving plates of the capacitor close together so that they do not move. Use your hand to pull the belt to move the pointer to the extreme left A of the square hole. When the capacitor is gradually turned out, the pointer gradually moves to the right. Now you can listen to the radio stations and record their frequency at the position pointed to by the pointer. After listening to dozens of places, you can completely draw the position of the frequency (or wavelength) on the white paper. After all the work is completed, a piece of mica can be nailed outside the square hole to avoid dust.

The size of this dial can be increased or decreased at will, but the length of the square hole must be slightly longer than half the circumference of the round wooden board. Ordinary radios are installed in wooden boxes, so although the materials of this dial are cheap, the outside is very beautiful after installation. When placed on a table, who wouldn't praise it?

Eighty Meters

— Cao Runsheng

Preliminary Shortwave Transmitter

This machine is simple in structure and easy to manufacture. Anyone who has made one or two radios will probably not fail. The vacuum tube used here is No. 31. Although the power is extremely small, it has a range of hundreds of miles thanks to the magic of shortwave. Because we want to keep the construction simple, we have adopted grid modulation. According to the actual results, it is not bad. If comrades are tired of playing with broadcast radios, then you may wish to try broadcasting according to this circuit.

Parts List

L Use hollow brass tubing (available at kerosene lamp stores), wind six turns on a three-inch diameter cylinder. After winding, remove from the cylinder and stretch by hand so that the distance between each turn is equal to the thickness of the wire.

Lr Wind twelve turns as above.

LLr is supported by four pagoda insulators.

CCr .00035 MFD air insulation variable capacitor.

C2 .002 MFD fixed capacitor.

C3 .00025 MFD fixed capacitor.

RFC High frequency choke coil. Self-made can use 28-gauge enameled wire to wind 200 turns on a one-inch diameter rubber tube.

T Modulation transformer. For self-made, you can use a phonograph transformer and add 400 turns of 28-gauge enameled wire on the outside as the primary (connected to the microphone). Connect the PH two heads to the phonograph head.

V Reference vacuum tube.

R Six ohm variable resistor.

A Battery Two volt storage battery.

B Battery 135 volts.

Microphone Battery 4.5 volt small flat battery.

After the whole machine is assembled, it can be tested. First connect the A and B batteries and clamp the clip near the fourth or fifth turn of the grid. Use another 16-gauge copper wire to wind a ring with a diameter of three inches, and connect a small light bulb to the two ends. Place this small light bulb close to Lr until the small light bulb lights up. If it does not light up, you can move the clip up or down until it lights up. In this way, the vacuum tube has oscillated. Then use a wavemeter in the 80-meter band and rotate Cr to make the small light bulb light up. At this time, the wavelength is accurate. Then you can connect the antenna and ground wire and rotate C. If the oscillation is good, the small light bulb will also light up. If it cannot light up, you can use a radio to listen at a distance of one or two zhang, and rotate C to make the sound received in the radio the clearest and loudest.

Improvements to Powerful Vacuum Tubes for Use as Detectors

— KMK

The main function of powerful vacuum tubes is generally to serve as powerful low-frequency amplifiers in the final stage (Power Amplifier), such as pentode powerful vacuum tubes like 25, 33, 39, 41, 42, 43, 47, etc. Because of their strong output coefficient between the screen and plate, they are used to increase the powerful audio output in the final stage. If ordinary vacuum tubes are used for two-stage low-frequency amplification, it is better to switch to a single-stage powerful low-frequency amplification, and the output volume is more than sufficient. Therefore, this type of vacuum tube is very popular among amateur researchers. However, in recent times, imaginative amateur researchers have been using powerful vacuum tubes as detectors, and circuit diagrams for powerful detection have been published in various newspapers and wireless radio magazines. Although the results are indeed excellent, there is always a disadvantage for every advantage.

Although powerful vacuum tubes used as detectors can achieve results exceeding any vacuum tube, the shortcomings are audio distortion and unstable feedback. Driven by curiosity, the author used a pentode powerful vacuum tube for detection in a regenerative single-tube radio. The results of the experiment were as expected. After several studies, it was discovered that the screen grid in the powerful vacuum tube is used to absorb electrons and strengthen the plate coefficient output. The instability of the feedback when used for detection is thought to be caused by the high screen grid voltage. Therefore, the arrangement method for a tetrode screen grid detection vacuum tube was adopted, and the results were unexpectedly good. The only improvement was adding two resistors to the screen grid. The circuit diagram is shown in the figure. Readers who share the same problem may wish to try adding the same modification.

Several Points to Note When Using Mercury Vapor Rectifier Tubes

— Yongyan

There are currently two types of rectifier vacuum tubes in general use: vacuum-type and mercury vapor-type (Mercury Vapor Rectifier). The latter is more effective than the former because the voltage drop of mercury vapor rectifier tubes is very small, usually about fifteen volts, and this voltage drop does not change with the load. In other words, using a mercury vapor rectifier tube can output a larger and more stable voltage. However, certain precautions should be taken when using them. These are briefly described below:

(1) The output current should not be overloaded. Each mercury vapor rectifier tube has a specified maximum output current (Maxim D.C. Output). If the current exceeds this limit during use, it will shorten the lifespan in the small case, and can cause damage in an instant in the large case. Some people often like to short-circuit B+ and B- with a screwdriver when testing a radio to see if there is a B voltage. This method is not a big problem when applied to a vacuum-type rectifier tube, but with a mercury vapor type, it can render it useless in a single move and should be absolutely avoided.

(2) The filament voltage must be as specified. The filament voltage of a mercury vapor rectifier tube must strictly adhere to the specified value. A voltage that is too high is certainly detrimental, and one that is too low can also cause the filament to age. Therefore, special care should be taken when designing the transformer that supplies the filament voltage. The filament voltage should also be measured at the tube pins, not at the transformer; because the filament current of rectifier tubes is often very large, the voltage drop on the wires is naturally also large and should not be ignored. At the same time, the tube socket should also have particularly good contact.

(3) After a mercury vapor rectifier tube has been idle for many days, before reusing it, the filament should be lit for about twenty seconds to evaporate any mercury particles that have condensed on it before applying the plate voltage.

(4) If the rectified current and voltage are very high, the filament current should be turned on for about half a minute first. Otherwise, if a high voltage is applied to the plate before the filament has heated up, the filament will be unable to cope and will be damaged.

(5) The voltage peak should not exceed the specified value. Each mercury vapor tube has a specified "Maximum Inverse Peak Voltant" (i.e., the maximum voltage that can be tolerated between the plate and cathode when the current is not flowing during rectification). This value should not be exceeded during use. (i.e., 1.4 times the voltage of the high-voltage coil should not be greater than this specified value.) For example, the maximum negative voltage peak of an 82 mercury vapor rectifier tube is 1400 volts. If used for full-wave rectification with 250 volts per plate, then 1.4 times the high-voltage coil voltage is 700 volts. This number is less than the specified maximum negative voltage peak, so it is known that there is no danger during use.

Also, mercury vapor rectifier tubes should be installed in a well-ventilated place to avoid excessive temperature increases, which could cause danger or damage other components.

Small Experiences

— Cai Rixin

When you have built a radio, you must check the circuit before inserting the vacuum tubes. The most important thing to pay attention to is the B+ circuit.

Single-Tube vs. Multi-Tube

It is absolutely essential not to connect it directly to the filament circuit. If connected incorrectly, vacuum tubes costing a few dollars each will be destroyed in an instant. The path of the B+ in ordinary circuits is mostly as shown in Figures 1 and 2. As long as the plate voltage is not misrouted, the vacuum tube will never burn out.

If you are still not sure after checking, you can turn on the resistor and connect the A and B batteries. Insert one end of the earphone into the F filament pin on the tube socket, and hold the other end in your hand, gently touching the other filament pin (it must touch the spring in the hole or the wiring post on the corner). At this time, there will be a "pop-pop" sound in the earphone. This sound is the same as the sound made when the two pins of the earphone touch the two poles of the A battery, which indicates that the wiring is correct and the vacuum tube can be inserted. If the "pop" sound is very loud, four or five times louder than usual, it indicates that the B+ has entered the filament. Do not insert the tube and re-check the wiring.

Figure 2: Multi-Tube

Membrane Protection Method

— Afeng

Ordinary radio earphones are necessary items, but due to prolonged use and the evaporation of heat inside the ear, vapor droplets form on the earphone membrane. People often like to wipe them off, which inevitably wipes off the black paint on the membrane, leading to rust over time and reducing the sound quality. This necessitates replacing the membrane with a new one, which is very troublesome. The following is a brief description of a protection method based on experimentation.

First, check whether the membrane is rusty. If it is in good condition, simply wipe off any dirt on the membrane with a soft cloth, then find two sheets of ordinary cigarette pack foil, cut them to the size of the earphone membrane, and place one on each earphone membrane (the foil must be flat and without small holes to be effective). In this way, even if water vapor appears, it will not damage the membrane.

If the membrane is already rusty, simply use the finest sandpaper to gently rub off the rust, then wash off the dirt with gasoline, and re-install the foil as before. Then, the sound will be as loud as when it was new.

Foreign News

Progress in Television

— Translated by Wang Fumin

Television (Television) seems unfamiliar in China, but it is almost universal in foreign countries, especially in Germany where progress is particularly rapid. The Lowe television receiver displayed at the recent German Radio Exhibition can be considered a perfect invention. This machine can not only receive moving images, but also receive sound simultaneously. The scanning line of the machine is up to 180 lines per inch, so the received image is very clear. The wavelength of the transmitting television set is 6.92m or 42900KC, which may be used in the future to 1cm. to 1m.

In recent months, the German Reichspost and Reichs Broadcasting Co. have jointly conducted several field television pickup experiments. They designed and built a television pickup car. Inside this car, sound movies can be filmed, and the four processes of developing, fixing, washing, and drying can be completed in one minute. This is truly an amazing feat.

Now the working procedure is described as follows: First, take outdoor scenes with a sound movie camera, and then complete the four steps of development, fixing, washing, and drying in one minute. Then it passes through a sound movie projector. In front of this machine, there is a Nikhow scanning disc and a photocell. When the film passes through this machine, it is immediately converted into light spots by the many small holes on the scanning disc, and then irradiated to the photocell and converted into current, and input into an eight- or nine-stage sensitive high-frequency amplifier, and then tuned to shortwave transmission and transmitted.

As for the receiver, it can be divided into two types in Germany: the first is for household use, and the screen is only eight inches high and ten inches wide. The second type is for public theaters, and the screen is as large as eight feet high and twelve feet wide. The imaging tube used in household television sets is a Cathode ray or Braun tube.

The Foreign Call Loan Rate Has Gradually Fallen 0.30 yuan in the Past Week

Since the start of the year, both the silver and money industries have been reluctant to make large-scale loans due to the fact that the Lunar New Year is coming soon, so although the market sentiment is gradually easing, the actual social situation is tighter than usual. As a result, all businesses are struggling, more than at any other time. Although the money supply has gradually recovered this time, the poor market sentiment ultimately makes it impossible to develop. The foreign call loan rate in the market was 0.23 yuan for both the morning and afternoon markets, which was 0.05 yuan less than the previous day. The interest rate was eight or nine points. In the call loan transaction, more than 2.2 million was transferred in the morning market, more than 600,000 in new transactions, more than 300,000 in afternoon transactions, more than 500,000 in small general meeting transactions, more than 400,000 in foreign pledged loan transactions taken back, more than 800,000 in new loans made, more than 500,000 in banknote recoveries, more than 700,000 issued, and 300,000 in unmarked notes, 100,000 in customer sources, and 250,000 taken in. Bank receipts and payments: foreign banks received and paid more than 2.2 million in bill money, more than 3.9 million in various goods, foreign exchange pledge and miscellaneous payments, more than 800,000 in foreign exchange settlements, more than 600,000 in special exchange payments, more than 400,000 in telegraphic transfers, and 400,000 entered the warehouse. Chinese banks received and paid more than 2.89 million in bill money, more than 4.34 million in various goods, exchange taxes, and miscellaneous payments, more than 700,000 in telegraphic transfers, more than 600,000 in special exchange payments, more than 1.22 million in foreign exchange settlements, and 600,000 exited the warehouse. Japanese banks received and paid more than 2.5 million in bill money, more than 3.3 million in various goods, exchange miscellaneous payments, more than 700,000 in foreign exchange settlements, more than 600,000 in special exchange payments, more than 300,000 in telegraphic transfers, and 400,000 exited the warehouse. The Securities and Bond Market Remains in a Sideways Trend

Yesterday, the Shanghai Chinese Merchants Securities Exchange and the market as a whole became increasingly stagnant after trending sideways. The overnight loan rate for foreign firms gradually eased, but investor sentiment remained unexcited. Although 20 million yuan would soon arrive in Shanghai, bullish sentiment was not enthusiastic, and arbitrage trading remained inactive. The crux of the problem was entirely due to the oversupply of shares. Large short sellers were not covering their positions and were even continuing to add to them. Retail arbitrage traders had not yet seen any swaps. Bullish longs and bearish shorts were strongly entrenched. According to some analysts, large short sellers, while not necessarily delivering all their shares, would undoubtedly have a significant number prepared for delivery. A prolonged sideways trend in the market was not beneficial for the bulls. Despite the sharp drop in the overnight loan rate for foreign firms, market prices did not rise. If the overnight loan rate were to rebound, market prices would undoubtedly fall. Although the money supply appeared loose on the surface, it was actually tight, and all industries would be contracting. Bankruptcies due to a lack of liquidity were being reported daily. The bond market, as the Lunar New Year approached, was affected by the sluggishness of all industries, making a rebound difficult. Currently, due to the easing of the overnight loan rate for foreign firms, the environment was favorable, and bullish sentiment was stable, so the market might continue to trend sideways. Yesterday's trading was generally listless. The opening and closing of both morning sessions showed declines of two or three cents. There were more sell orders for No. 78, with sell orders also for Nos. 16 and 53. However, all were lackluster. Although prices were weak, they did not fall. In the afternoon, the market resembled a flat line, and prices remained unable to rally. Prices for the front months were slightly firm, while those for the back months trended weaker, declining slightly by about one cent. At the close, only the Disbandment bonds were slightly firm, with the rest still down by about one cent. Prices might first decline slightly and then rise later. Yesterday's results showed a uniform decline of five cents to one cent and a half. The total trading volume was only 8,191,000 yuan. The Reason for the Sluggishness of the New York Stock Market

Japanese Overseas Bond Market is Softening

Xin Feng Foreign Firm reported yesterday (10th) that the New York stock market was sluggish and flat. Although commercial news was favorable, traders were unable to determine the market's future and were mostly taking a wait-and-see approach, waiting for a clearer trend before trading. Traders were also quite dissatisfied with the price action during the week, as they had originally expected the market to rise. Some sources expected continued declines before any rebound, but no one believed the market would collapse. The most important reasons for the current stock market stagnation were: (1) the impact of the Supreme Court's oil ruling remained in the market, and (2) the uncertain outcome of the Gold Standard. Due to financial difficulties, the Japanese bond market in London had softened, which was drawing close attention from traders here. The bond market was trending upward, and the situation on the small exchanges was stable. Chicago wheat rose slightly, with a total of 780,000 shares traded for the day. The Situation for Foreign Indian Rice is Getting Worse

Prices for each grade continue to fall by 0.03-0.10 yuan.

Speculators are seeking to sell their futures holdings, but the market is even more listless.

Yesterday, the foreign rice market suffered from ample inventories and a continuous influx of new shipments. Speculators were repeatedly lowering prices to liquidate their holdings, causing the market to decline step by step, becoming weak and listless. Spot prices continued to fall by 0.05-0.10 yuan, with significant differences in prices between grades. This was mainly due to oversupply in the market, allowing importers to take the opportunity to push prices down. After the price decline, over 40 bags were purchased by merchants from the mainland and local streets. Futures prices were being devalued by speculators, leading to an even more devastating situation. Prices had already fallen by 0.05-0.10 yuan, but speculators were still willing to lower prices to sell their holdings. New trading by foreign firms had come to a standstill, and 800 tons of returned goods were being offered. Indian rice was also being pulled down by foreign rice. Fortunately, there were fewer inventories on the market, and production costs were high, so the decline was limited to 0.03-0.05 yuan. A total of 4,500 bags were purchased by merchants from the mainland and local streets.

Factory Sales of Soybeans Suddenly Become Active

Yesterday, the soybean market was expected to continue the previous day's weakness and trend lower. However, oil mills suddenly increased their purchases, which stabilized sentiment. This was because factories saw that new shipments were not flooding in, inventories were decreasing daily, oil prices were firm, and cake sales were still active. Moreover, the Dachang New Oil Factory caught fire yesterday morning, resulting in one fewer supplier. Therefore, some factories intensified their work, leading to strong demand for soybeans. It is estimated that factories purchased over 5,600 bags of Guidetu soybeans, with prices ranging from 3.75 yuan to 3.72 yuan. Also, 25-26 trucks of Dalian Siping Street soybeans were purchased at a price of 4.00 yuan. Merchants from the inner city and local streets purchased over 2,000 bags of Hankou Zhazao soybeans, over 100 bags of Dalian Xicheng soybeans, over 200 bags of Yingzhou Chen soybeans, 200 bags of Hankou Didi soybeans, and 30 bags of Hangkou soybeans.

Southern and Northern Goods: There are Actually Reports of Shortages of Orchid Seeds

Recently, due to scarce supplies, the stock on hand for orchid seeds has gradually become thin. Moreover, according to a telegram from Tianjin, inventories have also been sold out, and there are predictions of a price increase of 1.00-2.00 yuan in the future market. Therefore, sales here have suddenly become active, but good quality all-yellow goods are extremely scarce. Out of necessity, people are settling for second best, so the price of ordinary goods has risen by 0.50 yuan, and good quality goods are also on the verge of running out.

Hardware: British Steel from Huisi is Running Out

The market for Huisi steel is currently strong due to the use of the steel by tobacco companies for making large boxes. As a result, existing inventory that had been accumulating for many days is being almost completely purchased. Prices are therefore gradually increasing. British steel is estimated at 27.00 yuan per 200 pounds, and American steel is estimated at 29.00 yuan. However, British steel is cheaper, so there are more buyers, leading to the current inventory on the market running out. It is reported that a total of 400-500 boxes (each box containing 200 pounds) have been sold in recent days, and the demand continues to be very active. However, due to the shortage of British steel, buyers are forced to purchase American steel, so the American steel market has been quite good in recent days. Therefore, there are hopes for further price increases.

Pure Antimony Prices are High, but Transactions are Rare

Pure antimony from Changning Shuikoushan in Hunan is widely used in the manufacture of bullets and other military supplies and lead type due to its excellent quality. Moreover, all countries (except Russia) need it. Therefore, exports are quite considerable each year. However, due to recent difficulties in transportation and the scarcity of production, prices have soared to 850.00 yuan per ton. Transactions, however, are slow because vendors find it difficult to sell. It is reported that only a few sales have been made in recent days.

Silk and Tea: Silk Prices May Increase

Shanghai: 13,000 dan of Raw Silk in Stock, 16,000 dan of Cocoons in Stock

In this week's silk market, the Shanghai users and speculators have been more enthusiastic than ever because Reuters misreported a 1.00 yuan price hike in New York, causing prices to increase. Though the report was later proven to be wrong, the price has not weakened because there are limited stocks of old silk in New York, approximately 13,000 dan of raw silk and 16,000 dan of cocoons in Shanghai and Wuxi combined. The quantity is only enough for the users' need. The market in Lyon has been fairly active these days. Some traders speculate the silk price might continue to increase.

Chekhov as an Impressionist

— Meng Jia

Chekhov, as a mirror of the Russian commoner intellectuals of the 1880s and 1890s, lived in such a chaotic era. On the one hand, the life of the aristocratic society was rapidly collapsing, and on the other hand, the bourgeoisie was gradually rising. However, at this time, the development of capitalism was still in the form of primitive accumulation, not yet mature enough for the bourgeoisie to realize its historical mission. On the other hand, the revolution advocated by the populist and People's Will intellectuals under the oppression of the landlord-bureaucrat Tsarist government had failed. Therefore, in this period of drastic change, the general intellectuals were at a loss and confused, "unable to grasp the consciousness of life, unable to overcome the chaos of life." As a result, they had to find spiritual self-anesthesia in Tolstoyanism; they loved to chat about "small events," limited their lives to the most trivial material concerns, and filled their lives with incoherent and meaningless rambling. They lacked a firm will, were easily moved, and were neurasthenic, "sometimes weeping and sometimes laughing wildly." They felt that their lives were "painful, blind, and dirty," and they also hoped to be liberated from this unbearable darkness and vulgarity, hoping to see a phantom of happiness. However, they were unwilling to make sudden changes—this would disrupt the balance of their lives—so their only way to escape was to die quietly.

They felt that "the colorful clothes of life had faded, leaving only some dim and mottled traces." They beautifully fantasized about the perfection of life three hundred years later, but they never thought, "Since everyone hopes so, who will realize it?"

Neurasthenia, easy to be moved, lack of a systematic thought and worldview, and misunderstanding of reality—these are the characteristics of Russian intellectuals in the 1880s. In this turbulent era, they lacked a systematic and fixed thought to analyze and synthesize objective reality, and could only passively and fragmentarily capture its impressions. In this atmosphere, Chekhov, as one of them, produced his impressionistic style.

Lunacharsky said in "We Should Criticize Chekhov":

"Chekhov's temperament is very weak, just like general artists, but he is a realist. His sharp eyes are constantly staring at his surroundings, with the fanaticism of a martyr, wanting to grasp all the reality. However, the complex and intertwined real life must be constantly observed sharply and expressed accurately. Chekhov did this… The real life of the era he lived in was rushing forward at the fastest speed. Chekhov unconsciously adopted the form of essays and short stories for his works, and even his dramas have this characteristic. His method of describing complex impressions is not general and holistic, but an uninterrupted chain of individual links… The emotions of impressionists are discrete and wandering, his pulse beats very fast, with neuroticism and feminine sensitivity—all these characteristics are the most true and most unique parts of Chekhov's style, and it is precisely because of these characteristics that Chekhov has moved towards new tracks and forms in literature and art."

Chekhov's impressionistic style, just like the general characteristics of Russian intellectuals in the 1880s, has its social basis. Due to the lack of a systematic thought—this can be seen in the process of Chekhov's ideological changes—and the ability to comprehensively understand objective reality, Chekhov—just like Russian intellectuals in the 1880s—could not understand objective reality in its entirety, complexity, essence, and direction. He could not systematically and comprehensively create a picture of the overall social life by melting and casting the life impressions he felt through the furnace of observation. He could only fragmentarily capture it—this also determined the form of Chekhov's works—the short story.

However, the reality embodied in Chekhov's short stories is by no means something separated from the entirety of reality, but rather "the impression of the whole dissolved," a fragment of the whole. Chekhov's short stories, "just like a powerful magnet and a photographic negative, fragments of life are gathered and condensed through it. Many of Chekhov's short stories and essays are full of a kind of lyric poetry—although this lyric poetry is often melancholy, and floats with a subtle contempt and sneer (not a comfortable cynicism, or the gentlemanly contempt of "Look, how shabby!," but rather a helpless contempt and sneer derived from sympathy and pity)—it is precisely this that is presented as one of the characteristic forms of the style of this impressionist.

Night Snow

— Yang Chen

The trembling sound of the whistle echoed intermittently in the ink-gray sky. Groups of three or five pigeons, carrying the dying shadows of the setting sun, circled around the bare branches, and then dispersed.

The sky had long been gloomy, but it became hazy and dark before five o'clock. The sparsely lit hutongs were darkly immersed in a yellow hue. The eerie night spread like a tide, accumulating the silence of the night.

Far away, the rustling of the wind gradually grew louder. It rolled up the yellow sand, howled and swept over, stirring up a sky full of smoke, but then rushed on.

The snow fell drop by drop, flying diagonally, flying onto the tiles, the branches, the black hutong alleys.

The sharp calls of the peddlers suddenly felt miserable. So desolate, like a cry of birth pains, swallowed up by the roaring wind. The lonely figure, bending over, staggered, walked past. Letting the snowflakes accumulate on his shoulders, the edge of his hat, and then fall off. But still walking slowly and steadily.

A cotton-covered carriage whizzed past with a "ding-dong" sound. The driver exhaled mist, panting up and down. The bright kerosene lamp broke through the surrounding dimness, and the icy bones of the ground grinned, revealing a pale face.

A blue, gloomy waning moon began to shed its dim light. The snow had already covered the rooftops. They reflected each other, turning into a pure white world. All the dark places were covered in white camouflage.

The low houses squatted docilely under the snow. The lazy dog had already hidden outside the old gate. The white hutong alleys stretched out like long snakes, twisting forward, disappearing into the corners of the walls.

Silence and paleness reigned over the city. Pedestrians wished they could shrink their heads into their scarves, exhaled a long breath, and immediately a cloud of smoke rose in front of them. Icy bones would congeal in their nostrils, and their ears would lose consciousness as if they were about to fall off from the cold. At this time, they would think of the South, think of warmth to comfort themselves.

Winter

— －Gcorge Wright

Monogamy

— Chen Fuxi

"Mommy, daddy... Hug, hug..."

This sound often pierced Wei Xuesheng's eardrums.

Wei Xuesheng rushed home from the company's office. As soon as he got home, he would hear the children cry, call for Mom and Dad, with no moment of peace. —Hearing the children's noise, Wei Xuesheng sank his tired body into a sea of depression. He hated the children, and even more he could not bear his wife becoming so thin and so hardworking because of these three "snotty kids." He worked in the office during the day, and in the evening, he should have enjoyed some family fun and adjusted his spirits. However, when he returned home, there was only a kind of miasma, a kind of disturbing noise.

"You're late coming home again today."

"Oh."

Wei Xuesheng stepped into the doorway, and his wife said this sentence as usual, and then said no more. His reply was also coldly indifferent. Having worked in the office all day, he was really tired at this time. He sat in a rattan chair, smoking a cigarette without any mood.

Silently, puffing out smoke.

"Children can ruin the happiness of a couple... A small family is best not to have children..." Wei Xuesheng thought.

He remembered that when they had no children, just after they got married, the house was clean and tidy, and only tenderness and sweetness filled the room. His wife was young, beautiful, and knew how to dress up. His wife's beauty and adornment often made Wei Xuesheng feel excited, and the fatigue of the day would often disappear when he saw his wife. They sat on the long chair every night, reading the evening newspaper, chatting, and joking, and no one would disturb them. But now, in order to manage three children and all the housework, his wife no longer had time to dress up. Her clothes were always so old-fashioned, and she didn't wear powder on her face, which was yellow and thin. Looking at her age, she seemed to be five years older than her original age. She was old, lost her graceful appearance, and completely became a poor housewife trapped in life. She no longer had time to sit on the long chair with her husband to chat, and never lightly joked with her husband. Her attitude became very serious, cold, and melancholy. Therefore, when Wei Xuesheng returned home and sat on that rattan chair, he was silent and only felt a bland taste, as if a dark cloud had covered his heart.

"Children can really ruin the happiness of a couple..."

Until the children cried, Wei Xuesheng, who was sitting in the rattan chair... Children are really demons who destroy happiness. Once there are children, the husband's love is completely transferred to the children. She only knows how to love the children and will no longer be considerate of her husband. She only pays attention to whether the children are cold or hot, and no longer pays attention to her husband's diet. A husband who has worked hard all day cannot get his wife's comfort when he returns home, and the mental deficiencies cannot be made up for by anything. Wei Xuesheng's lack of mental adjustment made him live in such a miserable and restless family, which was really painful.

Wei Xuesheng's spirit gradually became dull.

After giving birth to the third child, his wife separated from him. The husband's bed was set up in a dark corner of the room. After seven o'clock in the evening, Wei Xuesheng didn't read the newspaper or want to do any work, so he lazily went to sleep on that small bed. He got up early the next morning and slipped out of the house alone.

"Mom, I need to poop!"

"Mom! Mom!"

"Wah! Wah wah..."

Running out of the house, Wei Xuesheng heard the children call this every day. His heart froze like still water.

Distinguishing Characters and Distinguishing Words (II)

— Cao Juren

Host—It's a wonder that you are still a Chinese teacher, and you still laugh at the younger generation's Chinese proficiency getting worse and worse! You even say that you have never seen so many typos!

Guest—According to what you say, all your students are proficient in Shuowen and good at writing ancient characters!

Host—I say, if "typos" are only a unique problem of modern youth, then it is the youth's fault; if it is a common problem, it has been like this since ancient times, then you can't blame modern youth. You, old brother, a dignified Chinese teacher, also write and read typos, then you can't blame modern youth even more. Let me tell you: the problem of reading and writing typos has been the same for people three thousand years ago, two thousand years ago, and one thousand years ago. They are all the same, and no one deserves to laugh at anyone! In ancient times, reading and writing typos, Shuowen set a rule called "borrowing"; since "borrowing" is a common practice in using characters, why can ancient people borrow, but later generations are not allowed to borrow? There are two ways for ancient people to borrow, one is to borrow similar shapes, and the other is to borrow similar sounds. Young people are not proficient in Shuowen, but they have unintentionally embarked on these two ways of borrowing. For example, "stubborn" is written as "屈强" (qu qiang), "strength" is written as "疆弱" (jiang ruo), "intimidate" is written as "恐赫" (kong he), "obliterate" is written as "末杀" (mo sha), "fence" is written as "藩离" (fan li), "sharp edge" is written as "锋芒" (feng mang), "tremble" is written as "战栗" (zhan li), "observe secretly" is written as "司察" (si cha)... But they unintentionally wrote the correct characters, which are in line with the original meaning of Shuowen. In my opinion, before the Chinese characters are fundamentally reformed, the two rules of "borrowing similar shapes and borrowing similar sounds" will always apply, and we should not easily laugh at modern youth. Moreover, "converging," in the Biography of Wang Mang in the Book of Han is written as "四海辐奏" (sihai fuzou), "rewarding and encouraging," in the Biography of Wang Mang is written as "将劝" (jiang quan), "similar" in the Biography of Wang Mang is written as "疑似" (yisi). The value of the Biography of Wang Mang is inherent, and no one has ever laughed at Ban Gu, saying that his historical writing is diminished by typos! Think carefully, what is the relationship between modern youth writing a few typos and their Chinese proficiency? Let me tell you honestly, language and writing are relatively specialized subjects, if you don't understand something, it's best to keep your mouth shut!

Guest—Then, why is the Chinese proficiency of modern youth worse than before?

Host—Old brother, here you go again, who said that the Chinese proficiency of modern youth is worse than before? I don't think you have even read Zhang Taiyan's Guogu Lunheng! What "before" are you talking about? Which modern writers are you referring to? If you are referring to the Eight Great Masters of the Tang and Song Dynasties, Han Yu, Liu Zongyuan, Ouyang Xiu, and the three Su, please first take a look at the On Style chapter of Guogu Lunheng. Zhang Taiyan, you have always admired him, saying that he is a great writer. He said, "Li Ao and Han Yu were constrained by Confucian words and could not fulfill their ambitions. Quan Deyu and Lu Wen and Sima Guang of the Song Dynasty could only discuss success or failure slightly. Ouyang Xiu and Zeng Gong liked to make grand statements, but were unable to respond to the enemy. They held the shortest argument! As for Su Shi and Wenzi, they were just petty flatterers!" If you take the Eight Great Masters of the Tang and Song Dynasties as models for young people's articles, would Mr. Zhang Taiyan agree? Are you saying that the Chinese proficiency of young people is not as good as before, or are you saying that the "reasoning" and "organization" are not as good as before? Or are you saying that the "rhetoric" and "sentence construction" are not as good as before? Mr. Zhang Taiyan also said, "The articles of the Wei and Jin Dynasties resemble the late Zhou in argumentation. Although the style is different, they adhere to principles, attack with order, maintain harmony in reasoning, and can be teachers for a hundred generations." He also said, "All arguments should be based on famous schools, not on the School of Diplomacy." It can be seen that articles are mainly based on thorough reasoning. (Yan Zhitui's article chapter also says, "Articles should be based on reasoning as the heart, tone as the bones, events as the skin, and beauty as the crown.") Let's put aside "rhetoric" and "sentence construction" for now, and just talk about "reasoning" and "organization." Those ancient people in your mind, the Eight Great Masters of the Tang and Song Dynasties, the Tongcheng School, the Yanghu School, etc., will definitely not be more brilliant than modern youth; as for those old antiques with beards who claim to be the orthodox of classical Chinese, they are definitely not as good as modern youth.

Guest—Okay, give me a few examples!

Host—Whether an article is coherent or not depends on whether the reasoning is correct or not; so old antiques also use words like "insightful" and "knowledgeable" when criticizing articles. You must first acknowledge this premise.

Guest—I acknowledge this premise.

Smile (III)

— Written by Lawrence, translated by Tang Xiru

The abbess, she had a large-featured face with several features like Matthew's own, trying desperately to suppress her laughter, but as he raised his bony, malicious chin to meet her eyes, the smile gradually spread across her face. She slowly lowered her head, lower and lower.

The young, pale nun suddenly covered her face with her sleeve, her body trembling. The abbess put her arm around her shoulder and murmured with that Italian sentimentality: "Poor little thing! Well then, cry! Poor little thing!" But beneath this sentimentality, the stifled laughter was still there. The strong, dark nun still stood there motionless, clutching her black rosary beads, but the silent smile could not be moved either.

Matthew suddenly turned his head to the side of the bed to see if his dead wife was watching him, a movement of fear.

Ophelia lay so beautiful, so touchingly, her pointed, deathly white little nose pointing upward, her face a stubborn child's face, gazing at that final stubbornness. The smile disappeared from Matthew's face, replaced by the most sublime face of martyrdom. He did not weep; he merely stared blankly, his expression all the more melancholy: "I knew I had this idea of martyrdom in my heart!"

She was so beautiful, so childlike, so clever, so stubborn, so tired—and so still—all this seemed empty to him.

They had been married for ten years, and he himself had never learned well—no, no, never learned well at all. Ophelia always had her own will. She had loved him, then became stubborn and left him, and then eleven or twelve times became silent, or arrogant, or angry, but two or three times still returned to him.

Correction: The title of yesterday's novel (一) should be (二); and the (,) at the end of the last line should be (。); and the sentence "芒。芒禹迹" in the article "Distinguishing Characters and Distinguishing Words" has an extra (。). All corrections are made here, and readers are requested to pay attention.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talk

Talking About Pigs in the Year of the Pig

— Born in the Year of the Pig

Scolding can be considered a kind of insult. Even family members and friends can hurt feelings because of scolding. If I scold someone, the reaction will come immediately. If someone scolds me, how can I be willing to give up? But often things happen outside of the ordinary, such as this year, friends and family members are scolding me as a stinky pig, rotten pig, dead pig. Although it is said that this year is the Year of the Pig and I am born in the Year of the Pig, so the piglet is in charge and everyone is teasing, I still feel a bit insulted. However, I am not ashamed of it, and I accept it with a smile. Is it enduring humiliation? No, because I have a topic to write about because of this.

Since I admit that I am a pig, of course, I will start with myself as a pig. Whether I am stinky or not is not important. Perhaps I am usually too lazy to dress up, and I don't apply any Paris perfume essence, American duck egg powder, London beauty cream, or perhaps I ate chives and garlic and didn't hold a fragrant candy in my mouth, so that people's sense of smell fully feels unpleasant. It doesn't matter, because it is precisely because my pork is stinky and rotten that there is no danger of being sold, which is a great spiritual comfort. Although pigs are stupid, they are still honest. If someone calls me a tiger or a wolf, I will consider it a great shame and insult, and I will definitely negotiate and argue with them. In today's world, justice, peace, morality, and personality are almost completely destroyed by a generation of people like tigers and wolves. They are the world's greatest sinners. They are so vicious and lowly that they cannot be washed clean even under a waterfall. Although the pig is a weakling, it loves peace and will never have the ambition to invade others. Actions like going through walls and fences will not be done.

What is most pitiful and hateful is that people see pigs as honest and deceitful, and not only look at them with contempt, but also treat them particularly harshly, feeding them the leftovers and swill that people have eaten, and letting them live in simple, dirty, and wet places. Do people raise pigs for the sake of the pig's life? Dream on! Which pig farmer is not raising pigs for pork? Perhaps pigs do not know the brutal methods of humans. When the knife is thrown at their necks, they only understand, but they can only cry out once and shed a few tears to finish. Perhaps pigs have long known the tricks of humans, but they have always been regarded as livestock and dare not appeal to humans. Even if they cry out a few times, it will only hasten their death. I often have a fantasy, if the piglets can also clear their minds and cheer up a little, then the psychology of people despising piglets can be slightly reduced, right?

In the countryside, there is a kind of pig thief who is very skilled. He understands the psychology of pigs. Often in the middle of the night, he digs open the door of the pigsty and smears a pot of sweet sauce on the pig's mouth. At this time, the pig just stretches out its tongue to lick the sweet sauce on its mouth, and everything is left to the thief to arrange. Even its entire body is dragged out to the Shangdi Temple, killed, sold, and eaten. This certainly cannot be considered the honesty of the pig, but should be said that the pig is too foolish. It only knows that there is sweet sauce to eat at its mouth, but it does not know that this sweet sauce is the enemy's bait. However, this is one way of saying it. Try to observe the countless beings in the world, who doesn't want to taste some sweetness, but as a result, they lose their lives and remain ignorant. Then, I don't need to laugh at the pig's foolishness and gluttony.

Horse Carriage

— Zhou Han

Since arriving in Nanjing, I've enjoyed going out in a horse carriage. However, I prefer the open-topped carriages to the enclosed sedan-style ones. The sedan-style carriages don't allow you to see the scenery outside, like a prison van, which suffocates me. I don't like them. Open-topped carriages are so much more interesting. Along the way, I can admire the flying clouds in the sky, the azure mountains, and observe the roadside scenery and passing people. In Shanghai, you probably think riding in a car is the most comfortable, right? Actually, riding in a horse carriage is the most comfortable. Haven't you ridden in a horse carriage before? You don't believe me? Come on, take a trip to Nanjing sometime, spend two or three days, and I'll take you for a ride in a horse carriage. I guarantee you'll be very satisfied.

I also have a preference for horse carriages that differs from others. I don't like the galloping of swift horses and the speedy rush of new carriages. I prefer the slow, leisurely pace of old horses and old carriages. Are you laughing at me for being an idiot? You're the idiot. You need to know that I ride in a horse carriage to stroll around, not to rush. The slow pace of old horses and old carriages allows me to sit in the carriage, enjoy the scenery, and observe the roads. Moreover, when the carriage moves slowly, I can also chat idly with the coachman. Once, I hired a horse carriage to visit the Ming Xiaoling Mausoleum. Naturally, it was an open-topped carriage with an old horse and an old carriage. Coincidentally, the coachman was also a talkative old man. Can you imagine how enthusiastically he chatted with me? At first, he told me about his personal background and life, and later he even told me humorous stories.

But I've probably told you too much about horse carriages. Now, let me tell you about my visit to the Ming Xiaoling Mausoleum.

You've probably visited the Ming Xiaoling Mausoleum before. The scenery is as it was, nothing much to say. Let me tell you about a funny thing that happened to me. When I got out of the horse carriage and walked around the Ming Xiaoling Mausoleum alone, at first I only appreciated the autumn woods and colors, and didn't pay attention to anyone paying attention to me. When I got to the mausoleum area, a man followed me and even started talking to me. You might think I wouldn't be afraid of a man bothering me, but you'd be wrong. In that quiet, desolate wilderness, I started to feel scared. But the man wasn't particularly objectionable. He was just another "polite" gentleman. Although his suit wasn't very fashionable, it looked like he wore it very carefully—not to mention that his pants had a very sharp crease. At first, he praised me for being so brave, a woman visiting the mausoleum alone. Later, he even asked me what school I attended and where I lived. Of course, I didn't tell him. He said very politely, "Madam, (he really called me Madam,) your courage is extraordinary. You must be an outstanding talent, a female hero. I admire you very much. If you don't think it's shameful to associate with someone like me, please tell me your address so I can often visit and learn from you. It would be a great honor for me." You think I rejected his request, right? No, I told him my address. But I didn't tell him the truth. I lied. He also came by horse carriage. Later, his carriage kept following us. I got anxious. As soon as we entered the city, I switched to a rickshaw and slipped away.

Let me tell you, this time, it was like going on an adventure. But it was so interesting.

Vegetarianism

— Yonghui

His head was small and slender, a bit like the shape of a winter melon. His skin was pale yellow and dull, so dry it had no moisture. His eyebrows were high on his forehead, so far from his eyes that you'd almost suspect they were drawn on with ink. His eyes were close to his flat nose, and when he looked at people, his eyelids squeezed into a line. His entire face was very peculiar. Kong Fu was an old man who ate vegetarian food all his life.

It happened eight years ago, before I left my hometown. Kong Fu had also left a deep impression on my childhood.

One spring day, when all the flowers were in bloom, a group of naughty kids, including me, were playing around. We pulled at the flowers, caught flying insects. I was holding a featherless baby sparrow in my hand, playing with it, very happily.

"Amitabha! Why are you killing the sparrow?" A bony hand pressed on my shoulder. I quickly turned my head and saw Kong Fu's eyes squeezed into a line, staring intently at the sparrow in my hand. "Let it go. Accumulate good karma. Releasing life can cultivate merit for the next life." Without waiting for my reply, he snatched the sparrow from my hand, climbed up the tree trunk, and returned it to its nest. He was quite good at climbing trees.

Accumulating good karma was something young children didn't think about, and didn't even understand. What made me the saddest was that he took away my toy, and didn't let me kill it with a small tile. I howled and cried.

"Don't cry. I'll give you five copper coins." Tears stopped instantly. Five yellow copper coins had considerable power over a young child.

After that, whenever I caught any animal, I would deliberately let Kong Fu see it, so I could get a few copper coins to buy candy.

"Sister-in-law Bing, you're often sick and in pain. You should eat vegetarian food. Eating vegetarian food can eliminate illness and misfortune, and bring blessings to future generations." One afternoon, Kong Fu came to my house, chatting with my mother. He was a tenant farmer of our family.

"Old Fu, you really don't eat any fish or meat all year round?" My mother showed a skeptical expression.

"Of course. I made a vow before the gods." Kong Fu showed a proud look. "Don't even mention fish or meat, even if my lips touch a little bit of egg yolk, I'll throw up for a long time. I can't stand any meat. If I touch even a little bit, I'll throw up."

"Your sons don't eat vegetarian food, do they?"

"There's no way to make them listen," he said, looking a bit angry, lifting his piggy eyes to look at my mother. "I don't eat at the same table as them. Even the pots they cook meat in, I have to wash two or three times before I use them. I can't stand the smell of meat. If I touch a little bit, I'll throw up."

My mother asked Kong Fu to eat at our house.

"Sister-in-law Bing, what spices did you put in your tofu?" Kong Fu pointed at the bowl on the table. "Is it fried with sesame oil? It's really delicious!"

My fourth older brother made a face in the corner of the room, chuckling. I knew he was up to something again.

"Fourth brother, what are you laughing at?" I quietly walked over.

"Laughing at Kong Fu eating lard tofu!" He said in a very soft voice.

It's been many years since I returned to my hometown. Is Kong Fu still alive? Is he still persuading people to eat vegetarian food everywhere? His own stomach has already been filled with lard once. Does he know that?

Lao Chen's Disappointment

— Nan Yan

Following my appointment with Lao Chen, I hurriedly boarded the tram to C Park.

Walking into the park, I glanced around. It was deserted, without a single visitor.

"That makes sense, I'm late." I muttered to myself. So I listlessly strolled along the pond, passed through the artificial hill, and walked onto the soccer field. Almost half an hour had passed.

I kept looking towards the park entrance. There were some visitors coming in, but there was no sign of Lao Chen. I was so anxious that I almost wanted to run back.

Suddenly, a couple drifted in through the entrance. I immediately recognized the man as Lao Chen. I waved my hand in the air, and Lao Chen smiled and walked towards me, naturally with the woman.

After his introduction, I learned that the young lady was Miss Huang. I secretly glanced at Lao Chen's new friend. Her delicate, pretty face and those dark, shiny eyes were captivating. No wonder Lao Chen was chasing after her so desperately.

We walked a large circle in the park, crossing bridges, climbing hills, playing in the water, and rowing small boats. It was around eleven o'clock when we finally left the park and stepped into a quiet little restaurant. Although it was said to be a simple meal, the dishes on the table were tightly packed.

At the table, Lao Chen used all the skills he had to impress Miss Huang. Miss Huang's attitude towards him seemed very enthusiastic.

"Lao Chen's technique is really good! He can definitely hook her," I praised him silently.

In front of the small restaurant, I bid them farewell. As I left, I cordially invited them both to my apartment for lunch next week.

The day of the invitation arrived. I got up early in the morning and went to the restaurant to ask Lao Guan to send some more dishes.

After returning, I cleaned the apartment, sat down, and flipped through the newspaper, waiting for the guests to arrive.

Time really flies. The short hand of the clock on the table had already reached the middle of eleven and twelve, but the guests hadn't arrived. I was worried that they were too absorbed in their romance and hadn't heard me clearly, or that they had forgotten the date.

Therefore, I went over to my neighbor and called him. The person who answered the phone said he was not at home.

It was already twelve o'clock when I returned from my neighbor's house.

Suddenly, there was a knock on the door. I rushed forward and opened the door.

Lao Chen stood at the door, his face full of disappointment. The guest I was expecting was only him.

"Why didn't Miss Huang come with you?" I asked.

He walked into the room, immediately flopped down on the bed, and after a long while, said:

"Women are really unpredictable, damn it!"

Then he let out a long sigh.

After Eight Rounds

— Yi An

Amateur Mailbox

Limited and Unlimited Companies

Editor:

A long time ago, I often saw shop names like "XYZ Limited Company" or "XYZ Unlimited Company" everywhere, and I had a question: what is the meaning of "Limited Company" and "Unlimited Company", and what are the differences between the two? I really want to ask you to answer it for me, but I'm afraid that this question is not within the scope of your column's answers, so I dare not write a letter. Recently, I asked many people this question, but they couldn't give me a clear answer. I had no choice but to write to you, and I don't know if you can explain my question. Yours respectfully,

Wang Lvbingshang

Editor's Note: Regarding general common questions, as long as we know the answers, or we can find the answers elsewhere, we are willing to give our readers a clearer explanation. This is what we have said before, and it is also the purpose of this column.

There is a big difference between a Limited Company and an Unlimited Company. In short: a Limited Company is a joint-stock company; the liability of the shareholders who invested is limited to the capital they invested. For example, if there is a Limited Company with ten shareholders, each contributing 10,000 yuan in shares. If this company suffers a huge loss, even if the loss is more than 100,000, the liability of these shareholders is only 10,000 yuan. They are not responsible for any additional losses.

The shareholders of an Unlimited Company are different. These shareholders have unlimited liability. When the company suffers a significant loss, they not only lose their original capital, but also bear the responsibility of repaying all debts. A company organized in this way is called an Unlimited Company.
